Validity of Stipulating an Option for the Wife in Khul'
Intra-madhhab dispute on khiyar in khul'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on the validity of a khiyar clause in khul', compare their proofs, and identify the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
In khul', the wife cannot stipulate an option period — the relied-upon Hanafi position is that khiyar is invalid.

This passage presents a dispute within the Hanafi school: can a wife, when entering khul', be granted an option period (khiyar) to reconsider? Imam Abu Hanifa treated khul' from the wife's side like a sale, which permits option. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) disagreed, viewing khul' as an oath from both sides. The practical consequence is whether the divorce is immediate or can be rescinded. The relied-upon fatwa follows the Sahibayn.

Guided Path
1
Understand the scenario
The husband says 'You are divorced for one thousand on condition that you have an option for three days.' She accepts. Is the condition valid?
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and proof
Abu Hanifa: condition valid. Reasoning: khul' from wife's side is an exchange (mu'awadah) like a sale; option in sale is valid to prevent harm, and harm in personal matters is greater.
Qiyas to sale.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and proof
Sahibayn: condition invalid. Reasoning: khul' is an oath from both sides; oaths do not admit option. Also, option in sale is a concession (khilaf al-qiyas) and cannot be extended.
4
Identify the mufta bihi
The text states 'the three' (the three imams) agreed with Sahibayn, so the fatwa is on their view: no option for the wife; divorce is immediate and payment obligatory.
Although Abu Hanifa's reasoning is strong, the majority of the school adopted Sahibayn's position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صح شرط الخيار إلخ : أي إذا قال لها: "أنت طالق بألف على أنك بالخيار ثلاثة أيام" مثلاً فقبلت صح، ولو قال: "على أني بالخيار" لا يصح، وكذا إذا خالعها على ألف على أنها بالخيار ثلاثة أيام، فقبلت صح شرط الخيار، فإن ردت الخيار في المدة بطل الخلع ولا يقع الطلاق وإن اختارت فالطلاق واقع والمال لازم، وهذا قول الإمام؛ لأنه معاوضة من جانبها ويمين من جانبه، وقالا : لا يصح شرط الخيار لها بناء على أنه يمين من جانبها أيضاً، والطلاق واقع في الحال، والمال لازم عليها، وبه قالت الثلاثة فإن قلت: ثبوت الخيار في البيع على خلاف القياس فلا يقاس عليه غيره، قلت: أثبتناه هنا دلالة؛ لأن ثبوته في البيع إنما كان لدفع الغبن في الأموال، ولا شك أن الغبن في النفوس أضرّ، والحاجة إلى التروي فيه أكثر لهما أن الخيار للفسخ بعد الانعقاد لا للمنع من الانعقاد والتصرفان لا يحتملان الفسخ من الجانبين، والخلع لا يقبل الفسخ ؛ لأنه يمين من جانبه وشرط من جانبها، ولأبي حنيفة أن الخلع من جانبها بمنزلة البيع حتى يصح رجوعها قبل قبول الرجوع ولا يتوقف على ما وراء المجلس، فصح شرط الخيار لها، وأما في جانب الزوج يمين حتى لا يصح رجوعه عنه ويتوقف على ما وراء المجلس ولا خيار في الأيمان، والفرق بينه وبين البيع أن اشتراطه في البيع على خلاف القياس؛ لأنه من التمليكات، فيقتصر على مورد النص، وفي الخلع على وفق القياس؛ لأنه من الإسقاطات. (مستخلص، فتح)
The stipulation of option (khiyar) is valid, etc.: that is, if he says to her: 'You are divorced for one thousand on condition that you have an option for three days', for example, and she accepts, it is valid. And if he says: 'on condition that I have an option', it is not valid. Likewise, if he makes khul' with her for one thousand on condition that she has an option for three days, and she accepts, the stipulation of option is valid. Then if she rejects the option within the period, the khul' is void and no divorce occurs. And if she chooses [to accept], the divorce occurs and the money is obligatory. This is the statement of the Imam (Abu Hanifa) because it is an exchange from her side and an oath from his side. The two (Sahibayn) said: the stipulation of option for her is not valid, based on the view that it is an oath from her side as well, and the divorce occurs immediately and the money is obligatory upon her. And the three (imams) said this. If you say: the establishment of option in sale is contrary to analogy (qiyas), so other things cannot be analogized to it. I say: we have established it here by indication (dalalah). Because its establishment in sale was only to prevent harm (ghubn) in property, and no doubt harm in persons (nufus) is more severe, and the need for deliberation is greater. For them (Sahibayn): option is for rescission (faskh) after conclusion, not for prevention of conclusion, and these two actions (divorce and khul') do not admit rescission from both sides. And khul' does not admit rescission because it is an oath from his side and a condition from her side. For Abu Hanifa: khul' from her side is like a sale, so that her withdrawal before acceptance is valid, and it is not suspended beyond the session. Thus, stipulation of option for her is valid. As for the husband's side, it is an oath, so his withdrawal from it is not valid, and it is suspended beyond the session, and there is no option in oaths. The difference between it and sale is that stipulating it in sale is contrary to analogy because it is a transfer of ownership (tamlikat), so it is confined to the textual case. But in khul', it is in accordance with analogy because it is a relinquishment (isqatat). (Mukhtasar, Fath)
Source pages p. 473

Commentary
This passage presents a dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (and the three imams) regarding the validity of stipulating an option (khiyar) for the wife in a khul' contract. According to Abu Hanifa, if the husband says 'You are divorced for one thousand on condition that you have an option for three days' and she accepts, the condition is valid. During the option period, she may reject the khul' (voiding it) or accept (making divorce and payment binding). Abu Hanifa reasons that khul' from the wife's side is analogous to a sale (exchange), and since option is valid in sales, it should be valid here. Moreover, the need to protect against harm is greater in matters of the self than in property. The Sahibayn argue that khul' is an oath from both sides, and oaths do not admit option. They also note that option in sale is a concession (khilaf al-qiyas) and should not be extended. Abu Hanifa responds that khul' is a relinquishment (isqat), not a transfer of ownership, so it is actually in line with analogy. The fatwa is according to the Sahibayn that the option for the wife is invalid.

Key Terms
خيار (khiyar): An option period during which a party can rescind a contract.
إسقاط (isqat): A relinquishment or dropping of a right, such as in khul' where the wife drops her marital rights.
يمين (yamin): An oath; in this context, khul' is considered an oath (yamin) from the husband's side, and according to Sahibayn, from both sides.
معاوضة (mu'awadah): An exchange contract, like sale, where each party gives something in return.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, what is the ruling if a husband says to his wife 'You are divorced for one thousand on condition that you have an option for three days'?
A) The condition is valid, and she can rescind within three days.
B) The condition is invalid, and divorce occurs immediately with payment due.
C) The condition is valid only if the husband also has an option.
D) The khul' is void.

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that a wife cannot have an option period in khul' — the divorce is immediate and the payment obligatory.

The Three Hanafi Positions on Rights Waived by Khul' and Mubara'ah
Explains which marital rights are waived by khul' and mubara'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on what rights are waived in khul' and mubara'ah and apply them to a pre-consummation scenario.

Core Idea
In khul' and mubara'ah, the scope of waived rights depends on which Hanafi imam you follow.

Khul' and mubara'ah are forms of divorce initiated by the wife or by mutual consent, often involving financial waivers. The Hanafi school has a well-known internal dispute: do these agreements automatically waive all marital financial rights, or only those explicitly mentioned? This lesson unpacks the three positions held by Abu Hanifa, Muhammad al-Shaybani, and Abu Yusuf.

Guided Path
1
Understand the two terms
Recognize that mubara'ah implies mutual release, while khul' implies separation. Both can involve waiver of rights.
Both are forms of dissolution, but the legal consequences differ according to each imam.
2
Identify Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa holds that both khul' and mubara'ah waive all marital rights automatically, without needing specification.
Thus, after pronouncement, the dower and maintenance are entirely cancelled.
3
Identify Muhammad's position
Muhammad al-Shaybani holds that only the rights explicitly mentioned in the agreement are waived; unspecified rights, like dower and 'iddah maintenance, remain.
This means the wife can still claim the dower, and the husband can reclaim half if before consummation.
4
Identify Abu Yusuf's compromise
Abu Yusuf differentiates: mubara'ah waives all rights (like Abu Hanifa), but khul' waives only what is specified (like Muhammad).
This is based on the nature of mubara'ah as a mutual, absolute release.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويسقط الخلع والمبارأة المباراة مصدر باراً شريكه أي أبرأ كل واحد منهما صاحبه، و"بارأ الرجل امرأته" إذا برئ كل واحد منهما عن الآخر، فالمبارأة والخلع متساويان في أن كلا منهما يسقط به جميع حقوق النكاح أي الحقوق الواجبة بالنكاح من المهر والمتعة الثابتة عند الخلع مما لكل منهما على الآخر، حتى إذا كان الخلع والمباراة قبل الدخول وقد قبضت المهر لا يرجع عليها بشيء، ولو لم تكن قبضت شيئاً لا ترجع عليه بشيء، ولو خالعها على مال لزمها ويسقط الصداق؛ لأن هذين اللفظين يقتضيان براءة كل منهما عن صاحبه من حقوق العقد، وهذا عند الإمام، وعند محمد لا يسقط فيهما إلا ما سمياه فقط، ولها المهر على الزوج. وله الرجوع عليها بنصف ما قبضت قبل الدخول، ولا تسقط نفقة العدة إلا بالتسمية وبه قالت الثلاثة، وقال أبو يوسف له: تسقط بالمبارأة جميع حقوق النكاح كما قال أبو حنيفة رحاله، ولا يسقط في الخلع إلا ما سمياه كما قال محمد؛ لأن المبارأة تقتضي البراءة المطلقة من الجانبين؛ لأنها مفاعلة فهي وإن كانت مطلقة لكن قيدناه بحقوق النكاح بدلالة الحال، ومقتضى الخلع الانخلاع وقد حصل في نفس النكاح، فلا ضرورة إلى الانقطاع في الأحكام، ولأبي حنيفة: أن الخلع ينبئ عن الفصل، وهو مطلق كالمبارأة فيعمل بإطلاقها في النكاح وأحكامه وحقوقه، =
And khul' and mubara'ah drop [rights]. Mubara'ah is the verbal noun of 'he declared his partner free', meaning each of them released the other. And 'a man declared his wife free from liability' when each is clear of the other. So mubara'ah and khul' are equal in that each of them drops all marital rights, i.e., the rights obligatory by marriage, such as the dower (mahr) and the gift of consolation (mut'ah) established at khul', and what each has against the other. So if khul' or mubara'ah occurs before consummation and she has received the mahr, he cannot claim anything back from her; and if she did not receive anything, she cannot claim anything from him. And if he makes khul' with her for a property, it is binding and the dower is dropped, because these two words imply each of them being free from the other regarding rights of the contract. This is according to the Imam (Abu Hanifa). According to Muhammad, in both only what they specifically mention is dropped, and she has the dower from the husband, and he can claim back half of what she received before consummation, and the maintenance during 'iddah is not dropped unless specified. And the three (imams) said this. Abu Yusuf said: In mubara'ah, all marital rights are dropped as Abu Hanifa said, but in khul' only what they specify is dropped as Muhammad said. Because mubara'ah implies absolute release from both sides, as it is a mutual transaction (mufa'alah). Although it is absolute, we restrict it to marital rights by contextual indication. The import of khul' is separation (inkhila'), which has occurred in the marriage itself, so there is no need for cessation of obligations. For Abu Hanifa: khul' indicates severance, and it is absolute like mubara'ah, so it will be given absolute effect in marriage, its rulings, and rights. =

Commentary
This passage discusses the legal effect of khul' and mubara'ah on marital financial rights. There are three positions: Imam Abu Hanifa holds that both khul' and mubara'ah waive all marital rights (dower, mut'ah, etc.) without specification. Thus, if a khul' occurs before consummation and the wife already received the dower, the husband cannot reclaim it; if she didn't receive it, she cannot claim it. Any payment agreed in khul' is binding and the dower is waived. Muhammad al-Shaybani holds that only the rights explicitly mentioned are waived; unspecified rights remain, so she can still claim the dower, and the husband can reclaim half the dower if given before consummation. 'Iddah maintenance is not waived unless specified. Abu Yusuf takes a middle position: mubara'ah (being mutual release) waives all rights like Abu Hanifa, but khul' only waives specified rights like Muhammad. The relied-upon position is not explicitly stated, but the text mentions 'bi qalat al-thalathah' indicating the three (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad?) Actually it says 'wa bihi qalat al-thalathah' regarding Muhammad's position. The commentary suggests fatwa is according to Muhammad? Let's see: 'bi qalat al-thalathah' likely means the three (Abu Hanifa? No, the three might be Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and another? In context, it seems the 'thalathah' are the Sahibayn and another. But it says 'wa bihi qalat al-thalathah' referring to Muhammad's position. Actually the phrase 'وبه قالت الثلاثة' appears after mentioning Muhammad's position, so it means the three (probably Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and a third? But Abu Yusuf has his own view. Better not over-interpret. The passage is clear on the differences.

Key Terms
مبارأة (mubara'ah): A mutual release from marital rights, similar to khul' but with mutual consent.
صداق (sadaq): Mahr; the dower given by husband to wife at marriage.

A) All marital rights automatically.
B) Only the rights explicitly mentioned by the parties.
C) Nothing is waived; dower and maintenance remain.
D) Only the dower is waived, not the 'iddah maintenance.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the effect of khul' and mubara'ah on marital financial rights depends on which imam's view is applied: Abu Hanifa's absolute waiver, Muhammad's specification requirement, or Abu Yusuf's middle distinction.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Extinguishment of Marital Rights in Khul' and Mubara'ah
Explains the legal effect with intra-Hanafi differences.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad regarding the effect of khul' and mubara'ah on marital rights, and apply their rulings to determine the fate of dower and maintenance in given scenarios.

Core Idea
Khul' and mubara'ah extinguish all marital rights per Abu Hanifa, but only specified rights per Muhammad; Abu Yusuf splits the two.

When a marriage ends through khul' (wife-initiated divorce with compensation) or mubara'ah (mutual separation), all financial rights between the spouses are affected. However, the Hanafi imams differ on exactly which rights are extinguished. This lesson unpacks their arguments and the practical consequences for dower, maintenance, and other claims.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
The core question is whether khul' and mubara'ah automatically extinguish all marital financial rights (like dower and post-divorce maintenance) or only those explicitly mentioned in the agreement.
This is an intra-Hanafi disagreement, so all three imams are within the same school.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa holds that both khul' and mubara'ah extinguish all rights arising from the marriage contract. This means the dower (whether paid or unpaid) is dropped, and no maintenance during the waiting period is owed unless specified.
Key evidence: the word 'khul' means disconnection, so it is absolute like mubara'ah.
3
State Muhammad al-Shaybani's position
Muhammad holds that only the rights explicitly named in the khul' or mubara'ah settlement are dropped. If nothing is said about dower, it remains. Maintenance during the waiting period is not dropped unless specified.
This is the opposite of Abu Hanifa's position.
4
State Abu Yusuf's middle position
Abu Yusuf splits: mubara'ah extinguishes all rights (like Abu Hanifa), but khul' extinguishes only the specified rights (like Muhammad). The reasoning is that mubara'ah is mutual and implies absolute acquittal, while khul' is one-sided and limited to the compensation.
This is a compromise between the two extremes.
5
Apply to a scenario
Consider a khul' before consummation where the wife had already received the full dower. According to Abu Hanifa, the husband cannot reclaim anything. According to Muhammad, the husband can reclaim half. The mufta bihi (operative view) is Abu Hanifa's, but all views are recorded.
Know the thamarah al-khilaf: the practical difference matters in fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويسقط الخلع والمبارأة جميع حقوق النكاح أي الحقوق الواجبة بالنكاح من المهر والمتعة الثابتة عند الخلع مما لكل منهما على الآخر، حتى إذا كان الخلع والمباراة قبل الدخول وقد قبضت المهر لا يرجع عليها بشيء، ولو لم تكن قبضت شيئاً لا ترجع عليه بشيء، ولو خالعها على مال لزمها ويسقط الصداق؛ لأن هذين اللفظين يقتضيان براءة كل منهما عن صاحبه من حقوق العقد، وهذا عند الإمام، وعند محمد لا يسقط فيهما إلا ما سمياه فقط، ولها المهر على الزوج. وله الرجوع عليها بنصف ما قبضت قبل الدخول، ولا تسقط نفقة العدة إلا بالتسمية وبه قالت الثلاثة، وقال أبو يوسف له: تسقط بالمبارأة جميع حقوق النكاح كما قال أبو حنيفة رحاله، ولا يسقط في الخلع إلا ما سمياه كما قال محمد؛ لأن المبارأة تقتضي البراءة المطلقة من الجانبين؛ لأنها مفاعلة فهي وإن كانت مطلقة لكن قيدناه بحقوق النكاح بدلالة الحال، ومقتضى الخلع الانخلاع وقد حصل في نفس النكاح، فلا ضرورة إلى الانقطاع في الأحكام، ولأبي حنيفة: أن الخلع ينبئ عن الفصل، وهو مطلق كالمبارأة فيعمل بإطلاقها في النكاح وأحكامه وحقوقه، = كل حق لكل واحد على الآخر مما يتعلق بالنكاح حتى لو خالعها أو بارأها بمال معلوم كان للزوج ما سمت، و لم يبق لأحدهما قبل صاحبه دعوى في المهر
And khul' and mubara'ah invalidate all rights of marriage, i.e., the rights obligatory by marriage, from dower and enjoyment established at khul' from what each has against the other, such that if khul' and mubara'ah occur before consummation and she had taken the dower, he does not claim anything from her; and if she had not taken anything, she does not claim anything from him; and if he made khul' with her for property, it becomes binding on her and the dower is dropped, because these two expressions entail acquittal of each from the other from rights of the contract. And this is according to Imam (Abu Hanifa). According to Muhammad, nothing is dropped in them except what they specifically mentioned, and she has the dower against the husband, and he has recourse against her for half of what she took before consummation, and the maintenance during the waiting period is not dropped except by specification; and that is the position of the three (Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and al-Shafi'i?). And Abu Yusuf said: By mubara'ah all rights of marriage are dropped as Abu Hanifa said, but nothing is dropped in khul' except what they specifically mentioned as Muhammad said, because mubara'ah requires absolute acquittal from both sides because it is mutual; so even though it is absolute, we restrict it to rights of marriage due to contextual evidence; and the requirement of khul' is separation, and that has occurred in the marriage itself, so there is no need for disconnection in rulings. And for Abu Hanifa, khul' indicates termination, and it is absolute like mubara'ah, so it is applied in its absolute sense in marriage, its rulings, and its rights. = Every right each has against the other related to marriage, even if he makes khul' with her or makes mubara'ah for a known property, the husband gets what she named, and there remains no claim for either against the other regarding the dower.
Source pages p. 474

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof explaining the legal effect of khul' and mubara'ah on marital rights. It first states the general position of Imam Abu Hanifa, which is that both khul' and mubara'ah extinguish all rights arising from marriage, such as dower (mahr) and enjoyment (mut'ah) that were established at the time of khul'. This applies both before and after consummation. For example, if khul' occurs before consummation and the wife had already taken the dower, the husband has no claim against her for return; if she had not taken it, she has no claim against him. Moreover, if khul' is for property, it becomes binding and the original dower is dropped because these two expressions imply mutual acquittal from the rights of the marriage contract. The passage then presents the differing view of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, who holds that only the rights specifically mentioned in the khul' or mubara'ah settlement are dropped; any unmentioned rights remain, such as the dower, and the husband can reclaim half if it was before consummation. Maintenance during the waiting period (nafaqat al-'iddah) is not dropped unless explicitly specified—this is agreed upon by the three scholars (Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and al-Shafi'i, although the text says 'the three'). Imam Abu Yusuf takes a middle position: mubara'ah drops all rights like Abu Hanifa, but khul' drops only what is specified like Muhammad. The reason for the difference is that mubara'ah is a mutual agreement of acquittal, whereas khul' is a one-sided repudiation with compensation. Abu Hanifa, however, argues that the term 'khul' itself implies complete separation, so it should be treated as absolute like mubara'ah. The passage concludes that the effect is that once khul' or mubara'ah occurs, no claim remains between the spouses regarding the dower or other marriage-related rights.

Key Terms
الخلع (al-khul'): Divorce initiated by the wife in exchange for compensation (usually financial) paid to the husband.
المبارأة (al-mubāra'ah): Mutual agreement between spouses to separate, with both releasing each other from all claims.
البراءة (al-barā'ah): Acquittal or release from rights and claims.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, what is the effect of khul' on the dower if it occurs before consummation and the wife had already received the dower?
A) The husband can reclaim the dower from the wife.
B) The husband cannot reclaim the dower; it is dropped.
C) The wife must return half the dower.
D) The wife must return the entire dower.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the preferred view (mufta bihi) is that khul' and mubara'ah extinguish all financial rights between spouses, but Imam Muhammad and Abu Yusuf limit extinguishment to specified rights in khul'.

Talaq — Divorce

The Sixteen Scenarios of Khul'
Detailed enumeration of sixteen khul' cases

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to enumerate the sixteen scenarios of khul' and determine the financial consequences using the three variables: what is specified, timing, and receipt of mahr.

Core Idea
Khul' financial outcomes hinge on three variables: what is named, when the divorce occurs, and whether the mahr was received.

Khul' is a form of divorce initiated by the wife in exchange for compensation. The Hanafi school has meticulously categorized sixteen possible scenarios based on three key variables. This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq enumerates each case and provides the ruling, often distinguishing between qiyas (analogy) and istihsan (juristic preference). By mastering this classification, you will be able to apply the correct ruling in any khul' situation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three variables
Recognize that every khul' scenario is defined by (1) what compensation is specified (nothing, full mahr, part mahr, other property), (2) whether the divorce occurs before or after consummation, and (3) whether the mahr has been received or not.
These three binary choices combine to produce 4 (compensation types) × 2 (timing) × 2 (receipt) = 16 cases.
2
Trace the four compensation categories
The text first divides cases by what is specified: no compensation, the full mahr, a part of the mahr, or property other than the mahr. For each category, the timing and receipt of mahr further branch the rulings.
Each category yields four cases (2×2).
3
Analyze the 'no specification' cases (1–4)
When nothing is specified, the default rule (according to the correct view) is that each spouse is freed from obligations related to the marriage. This applies regardless of timing or receipt, except perhaps for minor variations noted in the text.
Case 1 is explicitly labeled 'as-sahih' (correct).
4
Analyze the 'full mahr' cases (5–8)
When the full mahr is specified, the ruling depends on timing and receipt. After consummation (case 6), the husband takes back all. Before consummation, received (case 7) leads to a conflict between qiyas (1500) and istihsan (1000). Before consummation, not received (case 8): qiyas gives the excess, istihsan gives nothing.
Note that case 7 and 8 introduce the qiyas vs. istihsan distinction, which is a hallmark of Hanafi fiqh.
5
Analyze the remaining categories (9–16)
For part of mahr and other property, apply the same logic: after consummation and received, the husband takes the specified part/property; before consummation and received, qiyas adds half the mahr while istihsan adjusts; when mahr is not received, it is dropped entirely. The husband's entitlement is limited to the specified compensation.
Memorizing the pattern for 'received' vs. 'not received' simplifies the entire set: if mahr is received, the husband may recover it fully or partially; if not, it is cancelled and only specified compensation is due.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الخلع

مقبوضاً كان أو غير مقبوض قبل الدخول بها أو بعده، وإن خلع صغيرته بمالها لم يجز عليها

أي المهر الخلع الصغيرة أي وسواء كان أي بالمرأة أي بعد الدخول الأب

قبل الدخول بها أو بعده: فهذا ينقسم على وجوه؛ لأنه إما أن لا يسميا شيئاً أو سميا المهر أو بعضه أو مالاً آخر، وكل واحد على وجهين: إما أن يكون قبل الدخول أو بعده والمهر لا يخلو إما أن يكون مقبوضاً أو غير مقبوض فالجملة ستة عشر وجهاً: الأول: أن لا يسمّيا شيئاً وكان الخلع قبل الدخول وكان المهر غير مقبوض برئ كل منهما عن حق الآخر مما لزمه في النكاح في الصحيح، الثاني: أن لا يسمّيا شيئاً وكان قبل الدخول، وكان المهر مقبوضاً، الثالث: أن لا يسميا شيئاً وكان بعد الدخول وكان المهر مقبوضاً، الرابع: هكذا والمهر غير مقبوض فالحكم في الصور الثلاث كالأول، الخامس: أن يسميا المهر وهو ألف درهم مثلاً والسادس: أن يكون بعد الدخول وكان مقبوضاً رجع عليها بجميعه بالشرط، والسابع: أن يكون قبل الدخول وكان المهر مقبوضاً فعليها بألف وخمسمائة ألف بالشرط وخمس مائة بالطلاق قبل الدخول قياساً، وبالألف المقبوض فقط استحساناً، والثامن: أن لا يكون المهر مقبوضاً يسقط عنه جميع المهر ويرجع عليها بالزائد قياساً ولا يرجع عليها بشيء استحساناً، والتاسع: أن يسميا بعض المهر بأن خالعها على عشر مهرها مثلاً والمهر ألف وكان بعد الدخول والمهر مقبوض، يرجع عليها بمائة درهم ويسلم الباقي لها، والعاشر: أن لا يكون المهر مقبوضاً يسقط عنه كل المهر مائة بالشرط والباقي بالخلع، والحادي عشر: أن يكون قبل الدخول والمهر مقبوض يرجع عليها بست مائة منها مائة بدل الخلع وخمس مائة بالطلاق قبل الدخول قياساً ويرجع بخمسين درهماً استحساناً؛ لأنه عشر مهرها قبل الدخول، والثاني عشر: أن لا يكون المهر مقبوضاً سقط عنه كله، والثالث عشر: أن يسميا مالاً غير المهر وكان بعد الدخول والمهر مقبوض فله المسمى لا غير، والرابع عشر: أن لا يكون المهر مقبوضاً فله المسمى ويسقط عنه المهر بحكم الخلع، والخامس عشر: أن يكون قبل الدخول والمهر مقبوض فله المسمى بالشرط ويسلم لها ما قبضت ولا يجب عليها رد شيء منه، والسادس عشر: أن لا يكون مقبوضاً فله المسمى بالشرط ويسقط عنه المهر بالخلع.
Book of Divorce. Chapter of Khul'. Whether [the mahr] is received or not received, before consummation or after, and if he performs khul' with his minor daughter using her property, it is not valid for her. (Commentary: meaning the mahr, the khul' of the minor, meaning whether it is, meaning for the woman, meaning after consummation, the father) Before consummation or after: this is divided into categories; because either they do not specify anything, or they specify the mahr or part of it or other property, and each of these is two types: either before consummation or after, and the mahr is either received or not received. So total sixteen cases: First: that they do not specify anything and the khul' was before consummation and the mahr was not received: each is free from the other's right regarding what was owed in the marriage, in the correct view. Second: that they do not specify anything and it was before consummation and the mahr was received. Third: that they do not specify anything and it was after consummation and the mahr was received. Fourth: similarly with the mahr not received. The ruling in the three cases is like the first. Fifth: that they specify the mahr, e.g. one thousand dirhams. Sixth: that it is after consummation and the mahr was received: he takes back all of it by the condition. Seventh: that it was before consummation and the mahr was received: she owes one thousand five hundred - one thousand by condition and five hundred by divorce before consummation by analogy, and only the received thousand by istihsan. Eighth: that the mahr is not received: all the mahr is dropped, and he takes back the excess by analogy, and he does not take back anything by istihsan. Ninth: that they specify part of the mahr, e.g. she divorces for one tenth of her mahr, and the mahr was one thousand, and it was after consummation, and the mahr was received: he takes back one hundred dirhams, and the rest remains for her. Tenth: that the mahr is not received: all the mahr is dropped - one hundred by condition and the rest by khul'. Eleventh: that it is before consummation and the mahr was received: he takes back six hundred - one hundred as compensation for khul' and five hundred by divorce before consummation by analogy, and he takes back fifty dirhams by istihsan because it is one tenth of her mahr before consummation. Twelfth: that the mahr is not received: all is dropped. Thirteenth: that they specify property other than the mahr, and it was after consummation, and the mahr was received: he gets what was specified, no more. Fourteenth: that the mahr is not received: he gets what was specified, and the mahr is dropped by the rule of khul'. Fifteenth: that it is before consummation and the mahr was received: he gets what was specified by the condition, and she keeps what she received, and she is not required to return anything. Sixteenth: that it is not received: he gets what was specified by condition, and the mahr is dropped by khul'.
Source pages p. 476

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the rulings on khul' (divorce by redemption). The author (the commentator) first mentions the matn statement that khul' applies whether the mahr is received or not, before or after consummation, and then notes the exception for a minor daughter. The main body of the passage enumerates sixteen possible scenarios of khul' based on three variables: (1) whether the parties specify no compensation, the mahr, part of the mahr, or other property; (2) whether the khul' occurs before or after consummation; and (3) whether the mahr has been received or not. For each scenario, the ruling on what the husband takes back (if anything) and what is dropped is given, often with a distinction between qiyas (analogy) and istihsan (juristic preference). The sixteen cases are: (1-4) no specification: in the first case (before consummation, mahr not received) both are freed from each other's claims; the next three (before consummation mahr received, after consummation mahr received, after consummation mahr not received) follow the same ruling. (5-8) specifying the full mahr: after consummation and mahr received, he takes back all; before consummation and mahr received, she owes the mahr plus half by qiyas, but only the mahr by istihsan; before consummation mahr not received, all mahr drops and he takes back the excess by qiyas but nothing by istihsan. (9-12) specifying part of the mahr: after consummation mahr received, he takes back that part; if mahr not received, all mahr drops; before consummation mahr received, he takes back the part plus half the mahr by qiyas, but only half the part by istihsan; before consummation mahr not received, all drops. (13-16) specifying property other than mahr: after consummation mahr received, he gets only that property; if mahr not received, he gets that property and the mahr drops; before consummation mahr received, he gets that property and she keeps the mahr; before consummation mahr not received, he gets that property and the mahr drops. The passage uses the terms 'qiyas' and 'istihsan' to indicate the preferred ruling in the Hanafi school. The teacher should note that these are detailed applications of the principle that khul' exchanges the mahr or other property for the divorce, and the timing affects pre-consummation claims.

Key Terms
الخلع (al-khul'): Divorce by redemption where the wife gives compensation to the husband to obtain release from the marriage.
المهر (al-mahr): The dower or bridal gift given by the husband to the wife as an obligation of marriage.
القياس (al-qiyas): Analogical reasoning used to derive a ruling for a new case based on an existing ruling due to a common effective cause.
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): Juristic preference that overrides qiyas for a more suitable ruling based on equity or public interest.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) One thousand dirhams
B) One thousand five hundred dirhams
C) Five hundred dirhams
D) Nothing

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has systematically covered all permutations of khul' financial consequences, with the mufta bihi typically being the istihsan ruling.

Khul' of a Minor Daughter: Father as Guarantor
Ruling on father performing khul' for his minor daughter with her property

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on a father performing khul' for his minor daughter, identify the condition of guarantee for the compensation, and distinguish between the father's and mother's authority in such a khul'.

Core Idea
A father's khul' on behalf of his minor daughter is valid only if he personally guarantees the compensation; otherwise, it is not binding on her property.

In this passage, we examine the Hanafi position on a father performing khul' for his minor daughter using her property. The key issue is whether the father's authority over his daughter's property allows him to unilaterally bind her to pay compensation. The passage clarifies that while the khul' itself effects a divorce, the financial side requires the father's personal guarantee. We will trace the rational proof for this separation and explore an intra-Hanafi dispute on the father's acceptance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and the Core Ruling
The act is a father performing khul' for his minor daughter using her property. The matn states it is 'not valid for her,' meaning the compensation is not binding on her. The divorce, however, does occur.
Distinguish between the effect on marriage (divorce) and the effect on property (no liability on the minor).
2
Locate the Proof (Dalil Aqli)
The commentator provides a rational analogy: just as khul' with wine (void consideration) still results in divorce but no financial obligation, similarly here the divorce is valid while the property does not become due from the minor. This proves the separation of rulings.
The proof is qiyas: comparing to khul' with wine.
3
Analyze the Condition of Guarantee
The passage introduces a scenario where the father says 'she is divorced, even if with one thousand dirhams, on condition that I am the guarantor.' Here the divorce occurs and the father owes the thousand. The guarantee makes the compensation binding on the father, not the minor.
The father's guarantee (daman) is the condition for the khul' to be financially effective.
4
Note the Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf on Father's Acceptance
If the father accepts khul' on behalf of the minor without guarantee, there are two narrations: one validates it, the other (the most correct) invalidates it because acceptance is like an oath and cannot be delegated. This dispute affects whether the minor's own acceptance is required.
The mufta bihi is that father's acceptance without guarantee is not valid; with guarantee it is valid.
5
Apply the Rulings to Different Scenarios
The passage also covers the mother's khul' (like a stranger), the discerning minor's own acceptance, and khul' for the mahr. Each scenario has distinct rules, all hinging on the guarantee condition.
Synthesize the rules: father with guarantee → valid; without guarantee → not binding on minor; minor's acceptance needed if mumayyiza.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

The stranger: is valid, so the father is more entitled, and occurrence [of divorce].
'And the one thousand is upon him': [meaning obligatory on the father; because stipulating the compensation of khul' for divorce with the father's acceptance. (A) It is said: the interpretation of the issue is that he performs khul' with her for other property like her mahr. As for khul' for her mahr, it is not permissible because the father does not have authority to cancel her ownership in exchange for something that is not valuable, and his guarantee in that is not considered. And the most correct view is that khul' for her mahr is like khul' for other property, and the father's guarantee of it is valid. And if the husband stipulates the compensation on her, it is dependent on her acceptance if she is eligible, i.e., if she is discerning, who knows that khul' is removing and marriage is bringing. If she accepts, it occurs by agreement; if she rejects the condition, the occurrence of divorce is relied upon without binding of property as previously. And if the father accepts on her behalf, it is valid in one narration, and not valid in another, which is the most correct; because her acceptance is like a condition of oath, which does not permit deputyship. And if he performs khul' for her mahr, it depends on her acceptance; if she accepts, divorce occurs, and nothing of the mahr is dropped as we mentioned; and if the father accepts, it is according to the two narrations as long as he does not guarantee it; and if he guarantees it, it is valid and divorce occurs because the condition exists, and her mahr is not dropped because it did not fall under the father's authority. Rami: 281/1] (Fath)
Source pages p. 476

Commentary
This passage deals with the khul' of a minor daughter (saghira) by her father. The matn states that if a father performs khul' on behalf of his minor daughter using her property, it is not valid for her. The commentator explains that the husband does not become entitled to the property named by the father, nor is the mahr dropped, because using her property is like a voluntary gift, which is not binding on her. However, the divorce itself occurs (as ba'in or raj'i according to earlier detail) because the divorce is separate from the financial obligation; even if the compensation is invalid (e.g., wine), the divorce still takes effect. The ruling is specific to the father; if the mother does it, it is like a stranger—valid only if she uses her own property and guarantees. Then the passage addresses a scenario where the father says: 'She is divorced even if with one thousand dirhams, on condition that I am the guarantor.' In this case, the divorce occurs and the one thousand is owed by the father. The father's guarantee is valid because he is assuming the debt, and the divorce proceeds. However, if the khul' is for the mahr itself, the father cannot unilaterally cancel the minor's right to the mahr; his guarantee is not effective for that. The minor's own acceptance is required if she is discerning (mumayyiza). If she accepts, divorce occurs; if she rejects, no divorce. The father's acceptance is disputed: in one narration it is valid, in another (the most correct) it is not, because acceptance is like an oath which cannot be delegated. Finally, if the khul' is for the mahr, the minor's acceptance is needed; the father's mere acceptance without guarantee does not suffice, but if he guarantees, it is valid and divorce occurs, though the mahr is not dropped.

Key Terms
الصغيرة (al-saghira): The minor daughter who is under the guardianship of her father and not yet legally capable of managing her own property.
الضامن (al-damin): The guarantor who assumes liability for the compensation in khul'; here the father guarantees payment on behalf of the minor.
المميزة (al-mumayyiza): A discerning child who can distinguish between beneficial and harmful acts, and whose acceptance is considered in legal matters like khul'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what happens if a father performs khul' for his minor daughter on condition that he is the guarantor of the compensation?
A) The divorce is invalid and the father owes nothing
B) The divorce occurs and the father must pay the compensation
C) The divorce occurs but the minor must pay from her property
D) The divorce is suspended until the minor reaches puberty

Key Takeaway
A father's khul' for his minor daughter effects divorce, but the compensation is binding only if the father guarantees it; without guarantee, the minor's property is protected and the father's acceptance alone is insufficient.

Khul' with Father's Guarantee for a Minor
Explains khul' with father's guarantee and conditions for validity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the validity of khul' performed by a father on behalf of his minor daughter and identify the effect of his guarantee on the divorce and financial liability.

Core Idea
A father's guarantee validates khul' for a minor, but his sole acceptance does not divorce her without the guarantee.

This lesson examines a key scenario in Hanafi family law: khul' initiated by a father for his minor daughter. The passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq clarifies when the divorce takes effect and who bears the financial compensation. Understanding the father's role and the importance of guarantee is crucial for applying the correct ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and the offer
The father makes an offer of khul' on behalf of his minor daughter, proposing a monetary compensation. Identify who is offering and who is accepting.
The text specifies 'she' refers to the minor daughter.
2
Recognize the condition of guarantee
The father must guarantee (daman) the payment. Without this guarantee, the divorce may not be valid. Distinguish between the father's acceptance and his guarantee.
The guarantee is a binding commitment to pay if the wife fails.
3
Distinguish between the two narrations on father's acceptance
One narration says the father's acceptance alone is valid; the most correct view (al-asahh) says it is invalid unless he guarantees.
The tarjih (preference) is based on the nature of acceptance as a personal condition.
4
Understand the effect on the mahr
If khul' is for the wife's mahr, the guarantee still works but the mahr is not dropped; it remains the wife's property.
The father has no authority to nullify his daughter's ownership of mahr.

Source Text

Chapter of Khul'. She is divorced even if for a thousand [dirhams], on the condition that he is a guarantor, she is divorced and the thousand is due on him. i.e., the minor. 'She is divorced' means the minor by the acceptance of the father according to the most correct [view]. (Ayni) 'Even if for a thousand' means even if the father made khul' for a thousand dirhams. (Ayni) 'Guarantor' for the thousand, meaning he is committed to it as a surety for her; because the property is not obligatory upon her. (Ayni) The stranger? Correct, so the father is more deserving and occurrence. 'And the thousand is due on him' means obligatory on the father; because stipulating the khul' compensation on divorce by the father's acceptance. (Ayni) It is said: The interpretation of the issue is that he makes khul' with her for other property like her mahr. As for khul' for her mahr, it is not permissible because the father has no authority to nullify her ownership in exchange for something that is not valuable, and his guarantee is not considered in that. The correct [view] is that khul' for her mahr is like khul' for other property, and the father's guarantee of it is valid. If the husband stipulates the compensation on her, it depends on her acceptance if she is eligible for it, i.e., she is discerning, one who knows that khul' removes [the marriage] and marriage brings [benefit]. If she accepts, it occurs by agreement? Rejection of the condition, and occurrence of divorce depends on it without obligation of the property as passed. If the father accepts on her behalf, it is valid in one narration, and not valid in another, which is the most correct; because her acceptance implies an oath condition which does not accept substitution. If the father accepts it, it is according to the two narrations as long as he does not guarantee it; if he guarantees it, it is valid and divorce occurs due to existence of the condition, and her mahr is not dropped because it did not enter the father's authority. Ramiuz al-Haqa'iq: 1/281 (Fath).
Source pages p. 477

Commentary
This passage from the chapter of khul' in Kanz al-Daqa'iq with its commentary (Fath al-Qadir) explains the ruling when a father makes khul' on behalf of his minor daughter with a guarantee. The matn states: 'She is divorced even if for a thousand dirhams, on the condition that he is a guarantor, she is divorced and the thousand is due on him.' The commentary clarifies that 'she' refers to the minor daughter, and the father's acceptance is valid according to the most correct view. The father is the guarantor for the compensation because the minor herself is not liable for property. The passage then discusses two scenarios: (1) If the husband stipulates the compensation on the wife herself, it depends on her acceptance if she is discerning. Her acceptance makes the divorce effective but she is not liable for the property because the condition was rejected. (2) If the father accepts on her behalf, there is a difference of narration: one view says it is valid, but the most correct view (al-asahh) says it is invalid because her acceptance is akin to an oath that cannot be delegated. Finally, the passage considers khul' for the wife's mahr. If the husband makes khul' for the mahr, it depends on the wife's acceptance; if she accepts, divorce occurs but the mahr is not dropped. If the father accepts, it is invalid unless he guarantees the mahr, in which case it is valid and divorce occurs, but the mahr remains due to the wife because it was not within the father's authority. The relied-upon position (asahh) is that the father's guarantee is valid and the divorce takes effect.

Key Terms
خلع (khul'): A form of divorce initiated by the wife in exchange for compensation (usually payment to the husband).
ضمان (daman): Guarantee or liability for the compensation amount; here the father guarantees the payment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Divorce does not occur because the father cannot accept on her behalf.
B) Divorce occurs and the father is liable for the payment.
C) Divorce occurs but the payment is not due on anyone.
D) Divorce occurs only if the daughter herself accepts later.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a father can effect khul' for his minor daughter only if he guarantees the compensation; his mere acceptance is insufficient.

Zihar: Definition, Conditions, and Ruling
Defines zihar, its conditions, and the prohibition of intercourse until expiation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of zihar, identify its conditions (who can perform, to whom, with what phrase), and explain the prohibition of intercourse until expiation.

Core Idea
Zihar makes intercourse haram until expiation: a husband likening his wife to a permanently forbidden female.

Zihar is a pre-Islamic custom that Islam regulated. It involves a husband declaring his wife like a permanently forbidden female relative (e.g., his mother), which immediately prohibits marital relations until he performs expiation. This lesson from Kanz al-Daqa'iq and its commentary Fath al-Qadir provides the precise definition, conditions, and ruling, along with the Quranic basis and notable intra-Hanafi differences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal definition
Locate the definition: 'It is likening the married woman to a [woman] forbidden to him permanently.' Break down the elements: the husband (subject), the wife (object), the comparison, and the forbidden female relative.
Note that the comparison must be to a woman, not a man, and the prohibition must be permanent.
2
Examine the conditions of validity
The text lists conditions: the husband must be Muslim, sane, adult; the object of comparison must be a permanently forbidden female (by lineage, fosterage, or marriage); the statement must be explicit (e.g., 'You are to me like the back of my mother' or equivalent). Identify who cannot perform zihar (dhimmi, insane, child, etc.) and note exceptions like the drunk or coerced.
The drunk's zihar is valid because he is still legally capable of speech.
3
Understand the ruling and its evidence
The ruling: intercourse and its preliminaries become unlawful until expiation is performed. The evidence is from Quran 58:3, which commands freeing a slave before touching. Note that the prohibition is temporary and conditional on expiation.
The expiation sequence is freeing a slave, then fasting two months, then feeding sixty poor.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi differences
The text mentions two disputes: (1) If a man likens his wife to a woman with whom he committed zina (e.g., his mistress's mother), Muhammad says it is not zihar, while Abu Yusuf says it is, based on enforceability of a judge's ruling. (2) If he kisses or touches another woman with desire before likening his wife to her daughter, Abu Hanifa says it is not zihar because the prohibition of those acts is textual, not analogous to intercourse.
These differences show the school's internal methodological debate on analogical extension.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

اتفاقاً
Chapter of Zihar. i.e. in explanation of its rulings. It is likening the married woman to a [woman] forbidden to him permanently, making intercourse and its preliminaries unlawful. i.e. zihar in the law. So no? i.e. to a forbidden woman? on the one who performs zihar? H like touching and kissing with desire? zihar. Chapter of Zihar: It is a verbal noun from zaahara yuzahhir. (Ayni) The connection between it and khul' is that zihar is also caused by the wife's nushuz (disobedience) as in khul'. Khul' was given precedence because it is more complete in prohibition by cutting the marriage, while zihar is a prohibition with the marriage remaining. Linguistically, it is facing back to back; when two persons have enmity, each turns his back to the other. It is said: zaahara min imra'atihi (he performed zihar from his wife) with 'min' although it is transitive by itself because it includes the meaning of distancing. (Fath) 'It is likening the married woman' is an idafah of the masdar to its object, i.e., the husband likening his married woman, meaning the husband who is Muslim, sane, adult, even if legally [so]; it is not valid from the dhimmi, insane, imbecile, bewildered, delirious, unconscious, sleeping, or boy. As for the drunkard, his zihar is valid, similarly the coerced, the mistaken, and the mute with his understood gesture. Its pillar is his saying: 'You are to me like the back of my mother' or what stands in its place. Its ruling: prohibition of intercourse and its preliminaries until the existence of expiation. He said 'married woman' unqualified, so it includes the case of a kitabi, minor, insane, whether entered or not, the slave woman, mudabbara, umm walad, mukataba, ajnabiyya (stranger), and the one divorced by one or three. (Fath) 'Zihar is valid only with a forbidden woman' i.e., to the one performing zihar, even if by rada' (fosterage) or musahara (in-law relationship). (Tahtawi) i.e., with a female who is forbidden to him. It means from the conditions of zihar relating to the object of comparison is that it must be from the kind of women. So if he says to her: 'You are to me like the back of my father or my son', zihar is not valid; because it is only known by revelation, and revelation only came concerning when the object of comparison is a woman, even if he intended zihar; and because the back of the father and son are not among the body parts that are forbidden to look at. (Fath with addition) 'Permanently' such as mother, daughter, and sister, to exclude a non-permanently forbidden [relative]. (Tahtawi, Ayni) The intent is permanence of prohibition by a description that cannot be removed, whether the prohibition is due to lineage, fosterage, or in-law. It is said that it should be extended to exclude the mother of the one with whom he committed zina and her daughter; because if he likened his wife to them, he is not a mazahir according to Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him), and according to Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on him) he is a mazahir based on the ruling that if the judge rules the permissibility of marrying them, it is enforceable according to Muhammad, contrary to the latter. If he kissed a woman or touched her with desire or looked at her private part with desire, then likened his wife to her daughter, he is not a mazahir according to Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him); and this is not similar to intercourse because its prohibition is textually established. Ramiuz al-Haqa'iq: 1/281 (Fath) 'He prohibited intercourse and its preliminaries' due to His statement, the Most High: 'And those who pronounce zihar from their wives' (Surah al-Mujadila: 3) up to His saying: 'So freeing a slave before they touch each other' (Surah al-Mujadila: 3). It was revealed concerning Khawlah bint Malik ibn Tha'labah, the wife of Aws ibn al-Samit. He saw her while she was praying, and she was beautiful. When she finished, he solicited her, but she refused, so he became angry and pronounced zihar from her. She came to the Prophet (peace be upon him) and said: 'Aws married me when I was young and desirable, and when he became old and my belly swelled, he made me like his mother.' And it is narrated that she said to him: 'I have children from him; if I gather them...'? Agreed?
Source pages p. 478

Commentary
This passage from the chapter of zihar (Kanz al-Daqa'iq with Fath al-Qadir) defines zihar and explains its conditions and ruling. Zihar is the act of a Muslim husband (sane, adult, capable) likening his wife to a permanently forbidden female relative (like his mother or sister). The legal definition emphasizes that the comparison must be to a woman, not a man. If he says 'You are like the back of my father,' it is not zihar. The object of comparison must be permanently forbidden, e.g., not a temporary prohibition like the wife's sister. The commentary details that the husband must be a Muslim, sane, adult; zihar is not valid from a non-Muslim, insane, child, etc., but a drunk or coerced person's zihar is effective. The ruling is that intercourse and its preliminaries (e.g., kissing with desire) become forbidden until the husband performs expiation (kaffarah), which the text mentions from the Qur'anic verse (Surah al-Mujadila: 3-4). The passage also discusses the story of Khawlah bint Tha'labah, which was the occasion of revelation. The commentary notes an intra-Hanafi difference: According to Imam Muhammad, if a man likens his wife to the mother of a woman with whom he committed zina, it is not zihar; but Abu Yusuf holds it is zihar because a judge's ruling on permissibility of marriage to such women would be enforceable. Also, touching or kissing another woman with desire before likening one's wife to her daughter does not constitute zihar according to Abu Hanifa, because the prohibition of such acts is textual, not analogous to intercourse. The passage ends abruptly with the story.

Key Terms
ظهار (zihar): A husband's statement likening his wife to a permanently forbidden female relative, making intercourse haram until expiation.
مظاهر (muzahir): The husband who performs zihar; must be Muslim, sane, adult.
كفارة (kaffarah): Expiation required for zihar: freeing a slave, then fasting two months, then feeding sixty poor.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is a condition for a valid zihar according to the Hanafi school?
A) The wife must be Muslim.
B) The object of comparison must be a permanently forbidden female relative.
C) The husband must pronounce it three times.
D) The wife must be present and consent.

Key Takeaway
Zihar is a serious prohibition that requires expiation before resuming marital relations; its validity hinges on the husband's statement likening his wife to a permanently forbidden female.

Zihar: Definition, Ruling, and Proof
Defines zihar, its conditions, ruling, and proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of zihar, identify its conditions, and explain why intercourse and its preliminaries are haram until kaffarah, using the Quranic proof and addressing the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Zihar makes the wife like a mahram – intercourse and even a kiss are haram until kaffarah lifts the bar.

Zihar is a pre-Islamic custom that Islam regulated. It is not a divorce but a temporary prohibition that forces a husband to choose between paying a heavy expiation or remaining separated. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi definition, the conditions for a valid zihar, the ruling of prohibition, and the proof from the Quran and Sunnah. We will also explore why the Hanafi school holds that even preliminaries to intercourse are forbidden, contrary to the Shafi'i view.

Guided Path
1
Define the act of zihar
Identify the essential components: the husband, the wife, the likening phrase, and the permanently prohibited woman. Understand that the phrase must explicitly compare the wife to a mahram by lineage, suckling, or marriage affinity.
The likening to a non-mahram (e.g., 'like my sister's back') does not constitute zihar.
2
State the ruling
The direct consequence of a valid zihar is that intercourse and its preliminaries become haram until the husband performs kaffarah (freeing a slave, fasting two months, or feeding sixty poor). The prohibition lifts only after the kaffarah is completed.
Zihar itself does not dissolve the marriage; it only imposes a temporary ban.
3
Locate the dalil
The primary evidence is Quran 58:1-4 (al-Mujadilah) and the hadith of Khawlah bint Malik. The verse commands kaffarah before the couple can 'touch' (tamass) again. Identify the operative word 'tamass' and its legal interpretation.
The imperative 'fa-tahriru raqabah' indicates obligation (wujub).
4
Analyse the wajh al-dalalah
The Hanafi position holds that 'tamass' literally means touching, and the Salaf understood it to include both intercourse and its preliminaries. Thus, the prohibition covers kissing, touching with desire, and looking with desire. The Shafi'i argument that 'tamass' is a metaphor for intercourse is rebutted by the fact that the literal meaning can be retained and combined with the metaphorical, especially when the matter concerns a prohibition where precaution is needed.
The principle of ihtiyat (precaution) in prohibitions strengthens the Hanafi view.
5
Note the ikhtilaf and tarjih
Imam al-Shafi'i (in his new view) and Imam Ahmad (in one narration) consider that only intercourse is forbidden, not the preliminaries. The Hanafi response uses linguistic reasoning and the hadith of Salama ibn Sakhr. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the Hanafi school is that all dawa‘i al-wat’ are haram.
The practical difference (thamarah): a Hanafi husband may not even kiss his wife after zihar until kaffarah, while a Shafi'i husband may.

(ع)] المناسبة بينه وبين الخلع أن الظهار يكون سببه النشوز أيضاً من قبل الزوجة كما في الخلع، وقدم الخلع؛ لأنه أكمل في التحريم بقطع النكاح والظهار تحريم مع بقائه، وهو لغة: مقابلة الظهر بالظهر، فإن الشخصين إذا كان بينهما عداوة يجعل كل منهما ظهره إلى ظهر الآخر، ويقال: ظاهر من امرأته بتعديته بـ"من" مع أنه متعد بنفسه لتضمنه معنى التبعيد (فتح) هو تشبيه المنكوحة: من إضافة المصدر إلى مفعوله أي تشبيه الزوج منكوحته أي الزوج المسلم العاقل البالغ ولو حكماً، فلا يصح الذمي والمجنون والمعتوه والمدهوش والمبرسم والمغمى عليه والنائم والصبي، أما السكران فيصح ظهاره، وكذا المكره والمخطئ والأخرس بإشارته المفهومة وركنه قوله أنت عليّ كظهر أمّي أو ما يقوم مقامه، وحكمه: حرمة الوطء والدواعي إلى وجود الكفارة، وأطلق المنكوحة فعمّ ما لو كانت كتابية أو صغيرة أو مجنونة مدخولاً بها أولا، الأمة والمدبرة وأم الولد والمكاتبة والأجنبية والمبانة بواحدة أو ثلاث. (فتح) الظهار من يصح بمحرمة عليه: [ أي على المظاهر المشبه ولو برضاع أو مصاهرة. (ط)] أي بأنثى محرمة عليه يعني من شرائط الظهار التي ترجع إلى المظاهر به أن يكون من جنس النساء حتى لو قال لها : أنت علي كظهر أبي أو ابني لا يصح الظهار؛ لأنه إنما عرف بالشرع، والشرع إنما ورد به فيما إذا كان المظاهر به امرأة وإن نوى الظهار، ولأن الظهر من الأب والابن ليس من الأعضاء التي يحرم النظر إليها. (ط، ع)] المراد تأبيد الحرمة باعتبار وصف لا يمكن زواله، سواء كانت الحرمة على المظاهر بنسب أو رضاع أو مصاهرة، وقيل: ينبغي أن يزاد لتخرج أم المزنى بها وبنتها؛ لأنه لو شبه امرأة بهما لا يكون مظاهراً عند محمد له، وعند أبي يوسف حله: يكون مظاهراً بناء على أن القاضي إذا قضى بجواز نكاحهما ينفذ عند محمد خلافاً للثاني، ولو قبل امرأة أو لمسها بشهوة أو نظر إلى فرجها بشهوة، ثم شبه امرأته بابنتها لم يكن مظاهراً عند أبي حنيفة له، ولا يشبه هذا الوطء؛ لأن حرمته منصوص عليها رمز الحقائق: ۲۸۱/۱] (فتح) حرم الوطء ودواعيه: لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَالَّذِينَ يُظَاهِرُونَ مِنْ نِسَائِهِمْ ﴾ (القصص:۳) إلى أن قال: ﴿فَتَحْرِيرُ رَقَبَةٍ مِنْ قبْلِ أَنْ يَتَمَاسَّا (القصص:۳) نزلت في خولة بنت مالك بن ثعلبة، امرأة أوس بن الصامت، رآها وهي تصلي، وكانت حسناء، فلما سلّمت راودها، فأبت فغضب فظاهر منها، فأتت النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فقالت: إن أوساً تزوجني وأنا شابة مرغوب في، ولما خُليت شنأت ونثرت بطني جعلني كأمه، وروي أنها قالت له عليه: إن لي منه صبية إن ضممته - اتِّفَاقاً
إليه ضاعوا، وإن ضممتهم إلي جاعوا، فقال عليها: "ما عندي في أمرك من شيء"، وروي أنه عليه قال لها: "حرمت عليه فهتفت وشكت إلى الله تعالى فنزلت الآية، فقال عليها: "يعتق رقبة" فقالت: لا يجد، قال: "فيصوم شهرين متتابعين"، قالت: يا رسول الله شيخ كبير يموت من صيام، قال: فليطعم ستين مسكيناً" قالت: ما عنده من شيء، فقال: سأعينه بعرق من تمر فقالت: إني أعينه بعرق آخر، فقال: "أحسنت اذهبي وأطعمي ستين مسكينا" الحديث ودواعي الوطء حرام في الظهار والإحرام والاعتكاف والاستبراء، حلال في الحيض والصيام، وقال الشافعي في الجديد: الدواعي ليس بحرام؛ لأن التماس أريد به الوطء وهو مجاز فيه، فلا يراد به الحقيقة، ونحن نقول: التماس حقيقة اللمس باليد فيحمل عليه حتى يقوم الدليل على المجاز، أو نقول: إنه يتناول المجاز لفظاً، ويلحق غيره به بالقياس احتياطاً في موضع الحرمة وبمثله لا يمتنع الجمع بين الحقيقة والمجاز، وعن أحمد رحلته في رواية: لا تحرم الدواعي. (عيني، فتح)
Chapter of Zihar: It is the likening of a wife to a permanently prohibited woman, forbidding intercourse and its preliminaries. ... The verse was revealed concerning Khawlah bint Malik, wife of Aws ibn al-Samit...
Source pages p. 478

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, defining zihar and its conditions. The author begins with the lexical and legal definition, then states the pillars and conditions. The proof is the verse from Surah al-Mujadilah and the hadith of Khawlah. The passage also includes an intra-Hanafi dispute (Abu Yusuf vs. Muhammad regarding likening to a woman born from zina) and an inter-madhhab dispute with Shafi'i and Ahmad regarding whether preliminaries are haram. The Hanafi position is that they are haram, using istihsan and the principle of precaution in matters of prohibition.

Key Terms
ظهار (zihar): A husband likening his wife to a permanently prohibited woman (e.g., his mother) by saying 'you are to me like my mother's back' or similar.
عود (‘awd): The return to the wife after zihar by intending to resume marital relations, which triggers the obligation of kaffarah.
دواعي الوطء (dawa‘i al-wat’): Preliminaries to intercourse, such as kissing, touching, or looking with desire.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on a husband kissing his wife after pronouncing zihar but before performing the kaffarah?
A) It is forbidden and requires a separate kaffarah.
B) It is forbidden and requires repentance only.
C) It is permissible because kaffarah removes the prohibition.
D) It is makruh but does not require anything.

Key Takeaway
Zihar is a serious pronouncement that forbids intercourse and its preliminaries until the husband performs the prescribed kaffarah; understanding its conditions and consequences prevents both sin and confusion with divorce.

Intercourse Before Kaffarah in Zihar: Only Istighfar Required
Ruling with proof on zihar and intercourse before kaffarah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a husband has intercourse before kaffarah in zihar, explain the evidence from the hadith of Salama ibn Sakhr, and distinguish the Hanafi position from the views of Sa‘id ibn Jubayr and al-Nakha‘i.

Core Idea
No additional kaffarah is required for intercourse before kaffarah in zihar; only istighfar and abstention.

This lesson addresses a specific scenario in zihar: what happens if the husband has intercourse with his wife before he has performed the obligatory kaffarah? The Hanafi school, relying on a direct hadith, holds that no extra kaffarah is due, but he must seek forgiveness and refrain until the original kaffarah is done. We will examine the proof and compare it with minority opinions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act? A husband who has intercourse after zihar but before kaffarah. The Hanafi ruling: only istighfar, no extra kaffarah.
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith of Salama ibn Sakhr, reported by Abu Dawud, al-Tirmidhi, al-Nasa'i, and Ibn Majah.
The Prophet (ﷺ) said: 'استغفر ربك ولا تعد حتى تكفر'.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet commanded only istighfar and forbade repetition until kaffarah. He did not command an additional kaffarah, implying none is required.
If another kaffarah were needed, the Prophet would have mentioned it (delay of bayan).
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Sa‘id ibn Jubayr says two kaffarahs; al-Nakha‘i says three. Their basis is possibly qiyas or general principles.
The Hanafi response: the specific hadith overrides analogy.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The hadith is sound (zanni al-thubut but clear dalala). The silence of the Prophet indicates no extra obligation.
This is the mufta bihi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بـ أنت علي: أي بقول الزوج لامرأته أنت إلخ. (ط) استغفر ربه فقط [ أي لا تجب عليه كفارة أخرى. (ط)] وقال سعيد بن جبير: عليه،كفارتان وقال النخعي عليه ثلاث كفارات والحجة عليهما ما روي أن سلمة بن صخر حين واقع امرأته وقد ظاهر منها أتى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فقال: يا رسول الله! إني ظاهرت من امرأتي فوقعت عليها قبل أن أكفّر، فقال: "ما حملك على ذلك يرحمك الله" فقال: رأيت خلخالها في ضوء القمر، قال: "فلا تقربها حتى تفعل ما أمرك الله"، رواه الأربعة، وفي رواية: قال له: "استغفر ربك ولا تعد حتى تكفر"، ولو كان شيء آخر واجباً عليه لبينه عليه السلام له رمز الحقائق: ۲۸۲/۱] (فتح)
By 'You are to me...': meaning the husband says to his wife 'you are [like my mother's back]'. He seeks forgiveness from his Lord only [i.e., no other kaffarah is obligatory]...
Source pages p. 479

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, addressing the scenario where a husband has intercourse with his wife after pronouncing zihar but before completing the kaffarah. The relied-upon Hanafi position is that only istighfar (seeking forgiveness) is required, and no additional kaffarah. This is based on the hadith of Salama ibn Sakhr, who asked the Prophet (ﷺ) after such an act, and he was instructed to seek forgiveness and delay intercourse until kaffarah. The passage also mentions dissenting opinions from Sa‘id ibn Jubayr (two kaffarahs) and al-Nakha‘i (three), but the Prophet's silence regarding any additional obligation proves the Hanafi view.

Key Terms
استغفر ربه (istaghfara rabbahu): To seek forgiveness from Allah, i.e., repent for the sin of having intercourse before kaffarah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the obligation upon a husband who has intercourse with his wife after zihar but before performing kaffarah?
A) He must perform two kaffarahs.
B) He must perform three kaffarahs.
C) He must seek forgiveness and not repeat the act until kaffarah is done.
D) He must immediately divorce his wife.

Key Takeaway
In zihar, if a husband has intercourse before performing the kaffarah, no additional kaffarah is required; he must only seek forgiveness and complete the original expiation.

The Meaning of 'Awd in Zihar: A Comparative Analysis
Inter-madhhab dispute on the definition of 'awd in zihar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to compare the Hanafi definition of 'awd in zihar with those of Shafi'i, Maliki, and Zahiri schools, and explain the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) of each definition.

Core Idea
In zihar, the 'return' that triggers kaffarah is the husband's resolve to resume intercourse, not the act itself.

Zihar is a pre-Islamic form of divorce where a man says to his wife 'You are like my mother's back,' thereby prohibiting intercourse until he performs kaffarah (expiation). The Qur'anic verse (Q. 58:3) says 'then they return to what they said' (thumma ya'udoon lima qalu) and links it to freeing a slave. Scholars differed on what constitutes 'return' ('awd). This lesson examines the Hanafi position, its proofs, and how it contrasts with the views of Imam al-Shafi'i, Imam Malik, and the Zahiriyya.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
The legal question is: What exactly is the 'awd (return) mentioned in the zihar verse that makes kaffarah obligatory? The answer determines when the husband must perform expiation.
The dispute is about the condition (shart) that triggers the obligation.
2
State the Hanafi position and its evidence
The Hanafi school holds that 'awd is the husband's firm resolve to resume marital relations (istibahat al-wat'). Even without actual intercourse, the intention to return triggers kaffarah. Evidence: The verse links 'return' with 'freeing a slave,' implying that the prohibition is violated by the intention to break it. Also, the hadith of Salama ibn Sakhr supports this.
The Hanafi reliance on the literal meaning of 'awd as 'returning to the prohibited act'.
3
Present the opposing views
Shafi'i: 'Awd means keeping the wife after zihar for a duration sufficient to divorce, without actually divorcing. Maliki: 'Awd is the act of intercourse itself. Zahiriyya: 'Awd requires repeating the zihar statement. Each view relies on different interpretations of the verse and hadith.
Note that the Shafi'i view sees 'return' as revoking the implicit divorce intention, while the Maliki view focuses on actual intercourse.
4
Analyze the Hanafi rebuttal
The Hanafi response argues that 'return' must mean intending to violate the prohibition, because keeping her in marriage does not necessarily imply an intention to resume relations. The hadith of Salama shows that the Prophet (ﷺ) considered his action (intercourse) as the violation, but the Hanafi view focuses on the resolve that precedes the act.
The rebuttal hinges on the definition of 'return' as 'intended violation' rather than 'retention in marriage'.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Under Hanafi, if a man resolves to have intercourse but does not act, kaffarah is still due. Under Shafi'i, kaffarah is not due until he keeps her for a period without divorcing. Under Maliki, no kaffarah until actual intercourse. Under Zahiri, kaffarah only if he repeats zihar.
The difference directly affects the timing and occurrence of the kaffarah obligation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعوده عزمه على وطئها المظاهر المذكور في قوله تعالى: ﴿ثُمَّ يَعُودُونَ لِمَا قَالُوا الذي يستقر به وجوب الكفارة. (ط، ع)] اعلم أن نفس الظهار وحده لا يوجب الكفارة، وإنما تجب الكفارة بعوده بعد الظهار؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿ثُمَّ يَعُودُونَ لِمَا قَالُوا فَتَحْرِيرُ رَقَبَةٍ ﴾ (الممتحنة:٣) حيث واصل التحرير بالعود بعد الظهار، فعلم أن الموجب هو العود بعده، فإن لم يعد يخير الزوج بين أن يطلقها أو يعطي كفارته، والمراد بالعود استباحة وطئها لا العزم على نفس الوطء؛ لأنهم قالوا: المراد في الآية ثم يعودون لنقض ما قالوا ورفعه وهو إنما يكون باستباحتها بعد تحريمها؛ لكونه ضدا للحرمة، وقال الشافعي العود أن يمسكها بعد الظهار زمانا يمكن فيه إيقاع الطلاق. ولا يطلق حتى لو طلق موصولاً بالظهار لا يلزمه كفارة عنده؛ لأن العود النقض، فنقض الظهار في إمساكها نكاحاً؛ موجب هذا التشبيه أن لا يمسكها نكاحاً، وقال مالك: العود الوطء نفسه، والحديث المذكور يرد عليه، لأن وقالت الظاهرية: إن يتكلم بالظهار مرة أخرى، ولا يحرم وطؤها بدون الثانية، وهذا فساده ظاهر؛ لأنه لو كان -
And his return is his resolve to have intercourse with her... If he does not return, he is given the choice between divorcing her and giving the kaffarah...
Source pages p. 479

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute about the meaning of 'awd (return) in the verse on zihar. The Hanafi position is that 'awd means the decision to resume marital relations (istibahat al-wat'), not merely the act of intercourse itself or keeping her in marriage. Shafi'i defines it as keeping the wife for a duration sufficient to divorce, while Malik says it is the act of intercourse itself. The Zahiriyya hold that it requires repeating the zihar statement. The passage argues that the correct view is Hanafi, using the hadith of Salama and logical reasoning. However, the text is incomplete; the argument against the Zahiriyya is cut off.

Key Terms
عود ('awd): The husband's meaningful intention to resume marital relations after zihar, which makes kaffarah obligatory.
ظهار (zihar): A pre-Islamic form of divorce where a man says to his wife 'You are like my mother's back,' prohibiting intercourse until kaffarah is performed.
كفارة (kaffarah): Expiation: freeing a slave, fasting two months, or feeding 60 poor persons, required to lift the prohibition of zihar.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what exactly is the 'awd that obligates kaffarah in zihar?
A) The act of having intercourse.
B) The decision to have intercourse (even without acting on it).
C) Keeping the wife as a wife after zihar for a period.
D) Repeating the words of zihar again.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school defines 'awd in zihar as the husband's intention to resume intercourse, making kaffarah obligatory upon that intention alone.

Limbs and Relatives That Constitute Zihar
Defines which body parts and relatives make zihar effective when compared.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state which body parts and relatives trigger zihar under Hanafi law and apply the ratio legis to new cases.

Core Idea
Zihar is established by likening the wife to any permanently prohibited body part or relative.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq clarifies the scope of zihar by specifying which limbs and relatives are equivalent to saying 'like the back of my mother.' The Hanafi school expands zihar beyond the back to any body part that is unlawful to look at or touch, and to female relatives with permanent prohibition through blood or breastfeeding. The commentary also explains how expressions like 'your head' or 'your half' cover the entire body.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core definition of zihar
Zihar is the act of a husband likening his lawful wife to a permanently prohibited woman (e.g., his mother). The passage stresses that this meaning (ma'na) is key.
2
List the body parts that trigger zihar
The belly, thigh, private part, and any part that is prohibited to look at or touch count as zihar when compared. The hand and similar parts do not, as they are permissible to see.
3
List the relatives that trigger zihar
Sister, paternal aunt, milk-mother, and any permanently prohibited female relative. Temporary relatives (e.g., wife's sister) are excluded because they become permissible after divorce or death.
4
Apply the analogy to whole-body expressions
Saying 'your head,' 'your private part,' 'your face,' 'your half,' or 'your third' is treated as zihar because these parts represent the entire body by extension, similar to how divorce is applied to undivided parts.
This is by qiyas (analogy) to divorce rulings.
5
Recognize the Hanafi expansion
The Hanafi school expands zihar beyond the mere back to all permanently prohibited body parts and relatives, unlike some other schools that restrict it to the back alone.
