Commentary
This passage is from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqaiq, specifically the section on the expiation of zihar. The author explains that the primary expiation is freeing a slave, with the conditions that the slave must be free from defects that prevent full utilization. The author first gives the general ruling: the slave can be male or female, young or old, Muslim or non-Muslim. He then cites the Shafi'i position that a non-Muslim slave is invalid, and responds with the Quranic verse about kindness to non-combatants. The text then details specific defects: blindness, loss of both hands/thumbs/feet prevent validity; loss of one hand/foot from different sides does not; loss of both from same side does. Deafness, one-eyedness, and being a eunuch or missing ears are valid. Zufar's stricter view is rejected because the lost benefits are supplementary. The insane are invalid, but intermittent insanity is valid during lucidity. The overall principle is that only complete loss of a major benefit (like sight, grip, walking, reason) invalidates the slave; mere deficiency does not.

Key Terms
الظهار (al-zihar): A pre-Islamic form of divorce where a husband says to his wife 'you are like my mother's back', making her haram for him until expiation.
رقبة (raqabah): Literally the nape; metonymically a slave (male or female) because the whole person is named by the part.
الأعمى (al-a'ma): A completely blind person; freeing such a slave is invalid for kaffarah because the benefit of sight is absent.
الأصم (al-asamm): A deaf person who cannot hear; but if he can hear when addressed, he is valid.
الأعور (al-a'war): A one-eyed person; such a slave is valid for kaffarah.
الخصي (al-khasiyy): A eunuch; his freeing is valid according to the majority Hanafi position.
المجنون (al-majnun): An insane person; permanent insanity invalidates, but intermittent insanity is valid during lucid periods.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school validates a broader range of slaves for zihar kaffarah, requiring only that the slave not suffer a complete loss of a major benefit; deficiencies and even non-Muslim status do not invalidate.

Invalid Slaves for Zihar Expiation: Mudabbar, Umm Walad, and Mukatib
Ruling with proof on invalid slaves for expiation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a mudabbar, umm walad, and mukatib who has paid part of the kitabah are invalid for zihar expiation and explain why using the Quranic proof.

Core Idea
Expiation requires freeing a fully owned slave; those with partial freedom do not fulfil the command.

The Kanz al-Daqaiq matn lists three categories of slaves that cannot be freed for zihar expiation: mudabbar (promised freedom upon master's death), umm walad (slave mother of master's child), and mukatib (contract slave) who has paid part of the kitabah. The commentator explains that these slaves have already earned freedom from one aspect, so their servitude is incomplete. The Quranic verse 'fatahreeru raqabatin' (freeing of a slave) demands a slave with complete servitude, and freeing such a slave would merely expedite an already existing right, not create a new emancipation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The matn states that it is not permissible (la yajuz) to free a mudabbar, umm walad, or mukatib who has paid something for expiation. Identify that the ruling is that these acts are invalid for fulfilling the expiation obligation.
The ruling is negative: the expiation is not fulfilled by freeing such slaves.
2
Locate the dalil
The commentator cites the Quranic verse 'fatahreeru raqabatin' (Surah al-Mujadilah 58:3) as the primary proof. This is a clear divine command.
The dalil is a Quranic text with qati' thubut and zanni dalalah.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The word 'raqabah' (slave) is indefinite and general, implying a complete slave with full servitude. The mudabbar and umm walad have a prior claim to freedom (tadbir and motherhood), so they are not fully owned. Freeing them is merely expediting what is already due, not creating a new emancipation. Hence they do not fulfil the command.
Key principle: the command requires a complete act of freeing, not a partial or anticipatory one.
4
Identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf (if any)
For the mukatib, there is an alternative narration from Abu Hanifa that a mukatib who has not yet paid may suffice. However, the text here focuses on the case where the mukatib has paid something, and the ruling is that he is invalid.
The ikhtilaf will be explored in a later lesson; for now, accept the ruling as stated.
5
Evaluate the ruling's practical consequence
If a person frees a mudabbar, umm walad, or mukatib who has paid part of the kitabah for expiation, the expiation is not accepted, and they must free a different slave who is fully owned and has no prior claim to freedom.
The consequence is that the act must be repeated with a valid slave.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمدبر وأمّ الولد والمكاتب الذي أدّى شيئاً. عطف على قوله: "والمجنون" أي لا يجوز تحرير المدبر وأم الولد في الكفارة لاستحقاقهما الحرية من وجه بجهة أخرى، فكان الرق فيهما ناقصة، وقوله تعالى: ﴿فَتَحْرِيرُ رَقَبَةٍ﴾ يقتضي الكمال ويقتضي إنشاء من كل وجه، وإعتاقهما تعجيل لما صار مستحقاً لهما، فلا يكون إنشاء من كل وجه (فتح). والمكاتب الذي أدى شيئا من بدل الكتابة؛ لأنه تحرير بعوض (ع).
The mudabbar, the umm walad, and the mukatib who has paid something. [Commentary] This is attached to his saying: 'the insane one' i.e. it is not permissible to free the mudabbar and umm walad in expiation because they have earned freedom from one aspect by another means, so servitude in them is incomplete. And the saying of Allah Most High: 'So the freeing of a slave' necessitates completeness and necessitates creation from every aspect. Freeing them is expediting what has become due to them, so it is not creation from every aspect (Fath). And the mukatib who has paid something of the kitabah price because his freedom is with compensation (Ayni).
Source pages p. 484

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with proof regarding which slaves are not valid for freeing in expiation for zihar. The matn states that a mudabbar (a slave promised freedom upon the master's death), an umm walad (a slave mother of her master's child), and a mukatib (a slave who has contracted to buy his freedom) who has paid some of the kitabah price are not valid. The commentator explains the reasoning: mudabbar and umm walad have earned freedom from one aspect (the mudabbar through tadbir, the umm walad through motherhood), so their servitude is deficient. The Quranic command 'the freeing of a slave' (Quran 58:3) requires a slave with complete servitude, and freeing them would merely expedite what they already deserve, not create new freedom. As for the mukatib who has paid part of the kitabah, his freedom is with compensation (the remaining payment), so freeing him is not a complete gift. This ruling is based on the principle that expiation requires a perfect act of emancipation.

Key Terms
مدبر (mudabbar): A slave who has been promised freedom upon the master's death, making him free from one aspect.
أم ولد (umm walad): A female slave who has borne a child to her master, thereby earning freedom upon his death (in Hanafi view).
مكاتب (mukatib): A slave who has contracted with his master to buy his freedom by paying installments.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Because the mudabbar cannot be owned

Key Takeaway
Expiation for zihar requires freeing a slave with complete servitude; slaves with prior claims to freedom (mudabbar, umm walad, mukatib who has paid) do not fulfil the obligation.

Ruling on freeing a mukatib who hasn't paid and buying a relative for expiation
Explaining two cases where expiation is valid: mukatib with no payment and buying a relative

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on freeing a mukatib who hasn't paid and buying a relative for expiation, and evaluate the opposing Shafi'i arguments citing the relevant proofs.

Core Idea
Freeing a mukatib who hasn't paid or buying a relative for expiation is valid in Hanafi school; the purchase itself is the cause of emancipation.

This lesson examines two specific scenarios where the Hanafi school permits expiation through emancipation, while other schools object. Understanding the legal reasoning behind these rulings deepens your grasp of how the Hanafi school balances textual evidence and logical analogy. We will analyze the proofs for both sides and see why the Hanafi view is relied upon.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on each case
Identify the two cases: (1) a man frees a mukatib who has not paid anything, (2) a man buys a close relative with the intention of expiation. Both are valid in the Hanafi school.
2
Identify the opposing view and their proof
The Shafi'i school, along with Zufar, Ahmad, and Malik, holds both invalid. For the mukatib, they argue he has earned partial freedom through the kitabah contract, like a mudabbar or umm walad. For the relative, they argue kinship is the cause of freedom, so purchase adds nothing, and purchase and emancipation are contradictory.
Note the use of qiyas to mudabbar for the mukatib case.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response: the mukatib's freedom is conditional on payment; before payment, servitude is complete. For the relative, the hadith of 'Ali (ra) states that a son finds his father enslaved, buys him and frees him, making the purchase itself an emancipation. The fa' indicates immediate causation.
The Hanafi school prioritizes the literal meaning (zahir) of the hadith and applies istihsan to extend the ruling to gift, charity, and bequest, but not inheritance.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafis accept these acts for expiation; Shafi'is require a different slave. The ruling also applies to expiation of oaths.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The text declares the Hanafi view as the relied-upon position ('indana'). The tarjih is based on the strength of the hadith and the logical consistency of the Hanafi argument regarding conditional ownership.
Authoritativeness: the matn states the position clearly, and the commentary supports it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن لم يؤد شيئاً من مال الكتابة يجوز؛ لأنه تحرير من كل وجه. هذه المسألة أولى المسائل الثلاثة التي يأتي جوابها بقوله: "صح" أي لو أعتق رجل لكفارته مكاتباً لم يؤد شيئاً من مال الكتابة جاز عندنا، خلافاً للشافعي وزفر، لهما: أنه استحق الحرية بجهة الكتابة، فأشبه المدبر وأم الولد ولنا أن الرق قائم من كل وجه، والواجب تحرير الرقبة، وهو تصيير شخص مرقوق حراً وقد وجد، ولم يتمكن نقصان في رقه بالكتابة؛ لأن عتقه معلق بشرط الأداء، فلو علق عتقه بشيء آخر لم يثبت به الاستحقاق قبل وجود الشرط، فكذا هذا. (مستخلص، فتح) أو اشترى قريبه الذي يعتق عليه بالشراء مثل أبيه أو ابنه أو أخيه. هذه مسألة ثانية أي رجل اشترى قريبه ونوى بالشراء الكفارة يجوز عنها عندنا، وقال الشافعي لا يجوز، وعلى هذا الخلاف كفارة اليمين، وبه قال زفر وأحمد ومالك؛ لأن سبب العتق هو القرابة، فلا يكون الشراء تحريراً مطلقاً كما لو علق عتقه بالشراء، وهذا لأن الشراء إثبات الملك، والإعتاق إزالته، فلا يجتمعان للتضاد. ولنا: أن شراء القريب إعتاق؛ لقوله علي: "لن يجزي ولد والده إلا أن يجده مملوكاً فيشتريه فيعتقه"، والفاء للتعقيب، فيعتق بسبب الشراء كقولهم: سقاه فأرواه فجعل نفس الشراء إعتاقا؛ لأنه لا يشترط غيره، والحاصل أن الخلاف في الجواز وعدمه يبتني على أن علة العتق هي الشراء عندنا والقرابة عندهم. وعلى هذا الخلاف لو وهب له أو تصدق به عليه أو أوصي له به وهو ينوي به عن الكفارة والتقييد بالشراء إشارة إلى أنه لو ورثه ناوياً بالإرث الكفارة لم يكفه عنها حيث لا يجزئه؛ لأن الميراث يدخل في ملكه من غير صنعه، بخلاف الهبة والصدقة والوصية؛ لأن الملك بهذه الأسباب يحصل بصنعه، وهو القبول فيجزئه كالشراء. (مستخلص، فتح)
If he has not paid anything of the kitabah wealth, it is valid because it is freeing from every aspect. This issue is the first of the three issues whose answer comes with his saying 'valid' i.e. if a man frees for his expiation a mukatib who has not paid anything of the kitabah wealth, it is valid in our madhhab, contrary to al-Shafi'i and Zufar. For them: he has earned freedom by the means of kitabah, so it resembles the mudabbar and umm walad. And for us: servitude is established from every aspect, and the obligation is the freeing of a slave, which is making a person who is owned free, and this has been found, and no deficiency entered his servitude by the kitabah because his freedom is suspended on the condition of payment. So if his freedom were suspended on another condition, the entitlement would not be established before the existence of the condition, so likewise this. (Mukhtasar, Fath) Or he buys his relative who becomes free by purchase like his father or his son or his brother. This is a second issue: a man buys his relative and intends by the purchase the expiation; it is valid in our madhhab, and al-Shafi'i said it is not valid, and on this difference is also the expiation of an oath, and Zufar, Ahmad, and Malik said likewise. Because the cause of freedom is the kinship, so the purchase is not an absolute freeing, like if he had suspended his freedom on purchase. And this is because purchase establishes ownership and freeing removes it, so they cannot be together due to contradiction. And for us: the purchase of a relative is freeing due to the saying of 'Ali: 'A son cannot repay his father except if he finds him enslaved and buys him and frees him.' The fa' indicates immediacy, so he becomes free due to the purchase, like their saying: 'He gave him water and quenched him.' So he made the very purchase a freeing because it does not require anything else. The conclusion is that the difference in validity turns on whether the cause of freedom is purchase (in our view) or kinship (in theirs). On this difference also if he is gifted or given in charity or bequeathed to him and he intends it for the expiation - and the restriction to purchase indicates that if he inherits him intending the expiation by inheritance, it does not suffice him because inheritance enters his ownership without his action, unlike gift, charity, and bequest because ownership by these means occurs by his action (acceptance), so it suffices like purchase. (Mukhtasar, Fath)
Source pages p. 484

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding two cases: first, freeing a mukatib who hasn't paid anything; second, buying a relative with the intention of expiation. The Hanafi school holds both valid, while Shafi'i and others disagree. For the mukatib, the Hanafi argument is that since he hasn't paid, his servitude remains complete; the kitabah is only a conditional promise, and the condition hasn't occurred, so he is like any other slave. For buying a relative, the Hanafis rely on a hadith from 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) where the purchase itself is considered emancipation. The opposing view considers kinship as the cause, so purchase adds no new element. The text also extends the ruling to gift, charity, and bequest (valid) but not inheritance (invalid) because inheritance lacks the person's own action. This shows the Hanafi principle of requiring an active, voluntary act of emancipation for expiation.

Key Terms
مكاتب لم يؤد شيئاً (mukatib lam yu'addi shay'an): A slave who has contracted kitabah but has not yet paid any installment.
شراء القريب (shira' al-qarib): Purchasing a close relative (such as father, son, brother) who would become free by purchase.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the mukatib has not yet earned any freedom since the condition of payment hasn't occurred
B) Because the mukatib is already free due to the contract
C) Because the master can annul the contract
D) Because expiation requires a slave who has never been promised freedom

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school validates freeing a mukatib who hasn't paid and buying a relative for expiation based on the principle that emancipation requires an active voluntary act, and the purchase constitutes such an act.

Piecemeal Emancipation for Expiation
Explaining that piecemeal emancipation is valid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on freeing half a slave then the rest for the same expiation and identify the condition required for its validity.

Core Idea
Freeing a slave in installments for one expiation is valid if no intercourse occurs between.

This lesson addresses a practical scenario: a person frees half of his slave for expiation, then later frees the other half for the same expiation. Is this valid? The Hanafi school holds that it is valid, provided he does not have intercourse with his wife between the two emancipations. Understanding this ruling clarifies that expiation can be fulfilled through partial actions, as long as the overall objective is met.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
The act is freeing half a slave for expiation, then freeing the remaining half later. The ruling is that it is valid (sahih).
This is the third case in the matn, implying two previous similar cases.
2
State the Condition
The condition for validity is that there is no sexual intercourse between the two emancipations. This is agreed upon (bil-ittifaq).
If intercourse occurs, there is a dispute within the Hanafi school (covered in the next lesson).
3
Understand the Reasoning
The deficiency from the first emancipation is a direct result of that act. Since the first emancipation was done for expiation, completing it with the second emancipation fulfills the obligation of freeing a complete slave.
Analogy: like a sacrificial animal that gets a minor defect after dedication – it remains valid.
4
Apply the Analogy
The text compares this to sacrificing a sheep for udhiyah where the knife accidentally hits its eye. Despite the defect, the sacrifice is valid because the intention was for the act of worship.
This analogy reinforces that incomplete actions can be completed later.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أو حرّر نصف عبده عن كفارته ثم حرّر باقيه عنها صح. هذه المسألة الثالثة أي لو أعتق رجل نصف عبده عن كفارته ثم حرر النصف الآخر عنها يجوز، ومعناه إذا لم يجامع بين الإعتاقين بالاتفاق، وهذا لأنه أعتقه بكلامين والنقصان من آثار العتق الأول، والعتق الأول بجهة الكفارة، فصار كما لو أضحع شاة للأضحية فأصاب السكين عينها (مستخلص). عنها: أي عن الكفارة فإنه يجوز أيضاً؛ لأنه أعتق رقبة كاملة بكلامين فحصل المقصود به. (ع)
Or he frees half of his slave for his expiation, then frees the rest of him for it, it is valid. This is the third issue: if a man frees half of his slave for his expiation, then frees the other half for it, it is valid. Its meaning is when he does not have intercourse between the two emancipations by agreement. This is because he freed him with two statements, and the deficiency is a result of the first emancipation, and the first emancipation was for the expiation, so it is like if he sacrificed a sheep for udhiyah and the knife hit its eye (Mukhtasar). 'For it' i.e. for the expiation, it is also valid because he freed a complete slave with two statements, so the objective is achieved. (Ayni)
Source pages p. 485

Commentary
This is a ruling statement about a third valid case: a man frees half of his slave for expiation, then later frees the other half also for the same expiation. This is valid according to the Hanafi school, provided he does not have intercourse with his wife between the two emancipations. The reason is that freeing is an act that can be done in parts; the first half-freedom is a deficiency in the slave, but since it was done for expiation, it is acceptable, and completing it with the second half fulfills the obligation. The commentator compares it to cutting a sacrificial animal where a flaw occurs—it remains valid because the intention was there.

Key Terms
أضحع شاة للأضحية (adha'a sha'tan lil-udhiyah): A simile meaning that if an animal for udhiyah gets a defect accidentally, it is still valid because the intention was there.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The two emancipations must be done on the same day
B) The slave must be physically whole
C) There must be no intercourse between the two emancipations
D) The slave must not be a relative

Key Takeaway
Freeing a slave in installments for a single expiation is valid provided there is no intercourse between the acts.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Divisible vs Indivisible Emancipation in Zihar Expiation
Two intra-Hanafi disputes on partial emancipation for zihar expiation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn disagree on the validity of freeing half a shared slave for zihar expiation, and apply the principle of divisibility of emancipation to similar cases.

Core Idea
Emancipation is divisible according to Abu Hanifa; indivisible according to Sahibayn—this dispute governs the validity of partial freeing for expiation.

This lesson examines a classical intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the expiation of zihar. The key question: Can a person fulfill the requirement of freeing a slave by freeing half a shared slave and then purchasing the other half? Or by freeing half before intercourse and the rest after? Abu Hanifa says no; the Sahibayn say yes. The disagreement hinges on a fundamental principle: is emancipation (itq) divisible or indivisible? Understanding this dispute illuminates how Hanafi jurists derive rulings from usul principles.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two cases and the ruling in the matn
Read the source passage and note that the matn answers both cases with 'la' (not valid). Determine which position this represents—Abu Hanifa's view. Recognize that the Sahibayn differ.
The matn's brevity hides the dispute; the commentary reveals it.
2
Understand the principle of divisibility of emancipation
Abu Hanifa holds that emancipation can be done in parts (yatajazzā); each part frees only that portion. The Sahibayn hold that emancipation is indivisible—freeing part frees the whole slave immediately.
This usul principle has broad implications beyond expiation.
3
Analyze Abu Hanifa's argument for the first case
When the muzahir frees half a shared slave, that part is freed. When he then guarantees the partner's half, that half comes to him already deficient (the other half is already emancipated). Since emancipation is divisible, the full slave was never freed in a valid way before intercourse.
The deficiency transfers with purchase, voiding the expiation.
4
Analyze the Sahibayn's argument for the first case
Since emancipation is indivisible, freeing half immediately frees the entire slave, assuming the muzahir ultimately owns the partner's share through guarantee. The slave becomes fully free from the first act, so expiation is valid.
If the muzahir is insolvent, even the Sahibayn say it's invalid because the slave works for compensation.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
If a mufti follows Abu Hanifa, these methods are invalid; if he follows the Sahibayn, they are valid. Later Hanafi practice often prefers the Sahibayn's view for ease, especially for a layperson who may not know the divisibility dispute.
The matn's answer 'la' suggests Abu Hanifa's view is the default in the text, but fatwa may differ.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن حرر نصف عبد مشترك بينه وبين غيره عن كفارته. هذه المسألة أولى المسألتين اللتين يأتي جوابهما بقوله: "لا" أي لا يجوز عن الكفارة، فالمسألة الأولى: أن المظاهر حرّر نصف عبد مشترك وهو موسر، وضمن لشريكه نصف قيمته ثم حرر باقيه لا يجزئه عن الكفارة عند أبي حنيفة، وقالا يجوز؛ لأن الاعتاق لا يتجزأ عندهما، فبعتق جزء منه عتق كله فصار معتقاً كل العبد؛ لأنه ملك نصيب شريكه بالضمان، وهذا إذا كان موسراً وضمن نصيب شريكه فيكون عتقاً بغير عوض فيجزئه، وإن كان معسراً يسعى العبد، فيكون العتق بعوض فلا يجزئه عن الكفارة وله أن النقصان تمكن في النصف الآخر؛ لأن العتق يتجزأ عنده فتعذر استدامة الرق فيه، وهذا النقصان حصل في ملك الشريك فيه، ثم انتقل بالضمان ناقصاً، فلا يجزئه عن الكفارة، بخلاف ما إذا أعتق نصف عبده ثم باقيه؛ لأن ذلك النقصان لذهاب البعض بسبب العتق فجعل من الأداء، ولا يمكن ذلك هنا؛ لأنه لا أداء قبل الملك (عيني، مستخلص، فتح) باقيه وهو المسألتين، يعني رجل حرر نصف عبده عن كفارة الظهار، ثم جامع التي ظاهر منها ثم حرر باقيه يجزئه عن كفارته عندهما، وعند أبي حنيفة: لا يجزئه؛ لأن المأمور به العتق قبل المسيس فلم يوجد؛ لأن عتق النصف وقع بعد المسيس، وهذا مبني على أن العتق يتجزأ، وعندهما: يجزئه لعدم تجزئ العتق عندهما كما سبق فإعتاق النصف اعتاق للكل، فكأن إعتاق الرقبة قبل المسيس. (مستخلص، فتح)
And if he frees half of a slave shared between him and another for his expiation. This is the first of the two issues whose answer comes with his saying 'no' i.e. it is not valid for expiation. The first issue: the muzahir freed half of a shared slave while he was affluent, and guaranteed to his partner half its value, then freed the rest; it does not suffice him for expiation according to Abu Hanifa. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: it is valid because emancipation cannot be divided in their view. So by freeing a part of it, the whole becomes free. So he becomes free of the entire slave because he owned the partner's share by guarantee. This is if he was affluent and guaranteed the partner's share, so it is freedom without compensation, so it suffices. But if he was insolvent, the slave works to earn the money, so the freedom becomes with compensation, so it does not suffice. And for him (Abu Hanifa): the deficiency occurs in the other half because emancipation is divisible in his view, so it is impossible to maintain servitude in it. This deficiency occurred in the partner's ownership, then it transferred via guarantee in a deficient state, so it does not suffice for expiation, unlike when he freed half his own slave then the rest because that deficiency was due to the loss of a part by emancipation, so it is considered part of the payment, but that is not possible here because there is no payment before ownership. (Ayni, Mukhtasar, Fath) 'The rest' which are the two issues: i.e. a man freed half of his slave for the expiation of zihar, then had intercourse with the woman from whom he pronounced zihar, then freed the rest; it suffices for his expiation according to the two, but according to Abu Hanifa: it does not suffice because what is commanded is emancipation before intercourse, so it is not found because the freeing of the half occurred after intercourse, and this is based on the divisibility of emancipation. And according to the two: it suffices because emancipation is indivisible in their view, so freeing half is freeing all, so it is as if the emancipation of the neck occurred before intercourse. (Mukhtasar, Fath)
Source pages p. 485

Commentary
This passage presents two intra-Hanafi disputes between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). First case: freeing half of a shared slave (with partner), then guaranteeing and freeing the rest. Abu Hanifa says invalid because emancipation is divisible and the deficiency in the partner's share invalidates; Sahibayn say valid because emancipation is indivisible, so freeing half frees all, and the guarantee is a separate purchase. Second case: freeing half, then having intercourse, then freeing the other half. Abu Hanifa says invalid because the required emancipation before intercourse was not complete; Sahibayn say valid because freeing half is deemed freeing all from the start. These disputes hinge on the core disagreement: is emancipation divisible (yutajazza) or not? The text also notes that if the person is insolvent, the first case becomes invalid even according to Sahibayn because the slave must work, making it freedom with compensation.

Key Terms
يتجزأ (yatajazzā): Divisible; whether emancipation can be broken into parts.
ضمان (daman): Guarantee; paying the partner for their share.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, why is freeing half a shared slave and then guaranteeing the other half not valid for expiation?
A) Because the slave is not fully owned at the time of the first freeing
B) Because emancipation is divisible, so a deficiency occurs in the partner's share that transfers to the muzahir
C) Because the guarantee is a form of purchase, making the emancipation with compensation
D) Because the partner might refuse

Key Takeaway
The validity of partial emancipation for zihar expiation depends on the usul principle of divisibility of emancipation, causing an intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

The Divisibility of Manumission: Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Ẓihār Expiation
Explains three cases of slave manumission for ẓihār expiation with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three scenarios of partial slave manumission for ẓihār expiation and apply the principle of tajazzu al-‘itq to determine validity according to Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
The validity of freeing half a slave for ẓihār expiation depends on whether manumission is divisible – Abu Hanifa says yes, the Sahibayn say no.

This passage from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqāʾiq examines three scenarios where a man frees half a slave (or part of a jointly owned slave) as expiation for ẓihār, with the condition that the slave must be freed before marital relations resume. At the heart of the intra-Hanafi dispute is a fundamental question: is the act of manumission inherently divisible (tajazzu al-‘itq) or indivisible? Understanding this ikhtilāf clarifies when the expiation is complete and when it must be repeated.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
Recognize that the passage deals with the validity of partial slave manumission for ẓihār expiation when the freeing is done in two halves, with possible intercourse in between or with a jointly owned slave.
The core variable is the timing of intercourse relative to the freeing and the nature of ownership.
2
State the three scenarios
First: freeing half of one's own slave then the other half without intercourse (valid by agreement). Second: freeing half of a jointly owned slave with a partner (disputed). Third: freeing half, then intercourse, then the other half (disputed).
The first scenario is unanimous; the second and third contain the ikhtilāf.
3
Identify the principle of dispute
The principle is tajazzu al-‘itq: whether manumission is divisible. Abu Hanifa holds it is divisible (the parts are separate acts); the Sahibayn hold it is indivisible (freeing part frees the whole).
This principle determines the ruling for scenarios 2 and 3.
4
Apply the principle to each disputed scenario
For scenario 2 (jointly owned slave): Abu Hanifa says releasing half does not free the partner's share until guaranteed, and the deficiency invalidates expiation; the Sahibayn say the first half frees the entire slave once ownership is secured via guarantee. For scenario 3 (intercourse between halves): Abu Hanifa says the second half after intercourse violates the condition; the Sahibayn say the first half already freed the whole, so condition is met.
The thamarah al-khilāf is whether the expiation is valid or must be repeated.
5
Determine the muftā bihī
The text does not specify the relied-upon view, but later Hanafi works (e.g., al-Hidāyah) often adopt the Sahibayn's position due to its consistency with the principle of indivisibility and practicality.
Note that even in the first scenario, if the man is wealthy and owes the partner, the Sahibayn's view holds only when he is wealthy; if poor, the slave works for value and the expiation is invalid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطلاق بيان كفارة الظهار أو حرّر نصف عبده عن كفارته ثم حرّر باقيه عنها صح. وإن حرر نصف عبد مشترك لشريكه وهو النصف الآخر، أو حرّر نصف عبده ثم وطئ التي ظاهر منها ثم حرّر باقيه عنها، لا، فإن لم يجد ما يعتق صام شهرين متتابعين ليس فيهما رمضان أو حرّر نصف عبده : هذه المسألة الثالثة أي لو أعتق رجل نصف عبده عن كفارته ثم حرر النصف الآخر عنها يجوز، ومعناه إذا لم يجامع بين الإعتاقين بالاتفاق، وهذا لأنه أعتقه بكلامين والنقصان من آثار العتق الأول، والعتق الأول بجهة الكفارة، فصار كما لو أضحع شاة للأضحية فأصاب السكين عينها وإنما قيدنا بعدم الجماع بين الإعتاقين؛ لأنه لو جامع بينهما لا يجوز عتقه عن الكفارة عند أبي حنيفة، ويجوز عندهما كما سيأتي. (مستخلص) عنها: أي عن الكفارة فإنه يجوز أيضاً؛ لأنه أعتق رقبة كاملة بكلامين فحصل المقصود به. (ع) صح: جواب المسائل الثلاث أي صح تحرير المظاهر عن الكفارة في هذه المسائل. (ع) وإن حرر نصف عبد مشترك بينه وبين غيره عن كفارته. (مستخلص، فتح الله المعين باقيه: وهو النصف الآخر لم يجز أيضاً. (ع) لا: جواب المسألتين أي لا يجوز عن الكفارة. (ع) النصف الآخر بأن كان موسراً لم يجز ذلك. (ع) أو حرر نصف عبده إلخ: هذه مسألة ثانية من
The Book of Divorce. Explanation of the expiation for ẓihār. Or he freed half of his slave for his expiation, then freed the remaining half for it: valid. And if he freed half of a jointly owned slave belonging to his partner, which is the other half, or he freed half of his slave, then had intercourse with the one from whom he had made ẓihār, then freed the remaining half for it: no. But if he does not find what to free, he fasts two consecutive months in which there is no Ramadan. Or freed half of his slave: this is the third issue, i.e., if a man freed half of his slave for his expiation, then freed the other half for it, it is valid, meaning if he did not have intercourse between the two freeings by agreement. This is because he freed him with two utterances, and the deficiency is from the effects of the first freeing, and the first freeing is for the sake of the expiation. So the first issue: the one who made ẓihār freed half of a jointly owned slave while he is wealthy, and guaranteed for his partner half its value, then freed the remaining half: it does not suffice for the expiation according to Abu Hanifa, and they said it is valid because manumission is not divisible according to them. So by freeing a part of it, the whole becomes free, so he becomes a manumitter of the entire slave because he owns the partner's share by guarantee. This is if he is wealthy and guaranteed the partner's share, so it is a manumission without compensation, so it suffices. If he is poor, the slave works for the value, so it is a manumission with compensation, so it does not suffice for the expiation. He has (the argument) that the deficiency is established in the other half because manumission is divisible according to him, so it is impossible to persist in slavery in it. This deficiency occurred in the ownership of the partner in it, then it was transferred by guarantee deficient, so it does not suffice for the expiation, unlike the case where he freed half his slave then the rest, because that deficiency is due to the loss of a part because of manumission, so it is considered from the performance, and that is not possible here because there is no performance before ownership. The remaining half: i.e., the two issues, meaning a man freed half his slave for the expiation of ẓihār, then had intercourse with the one from whom he made ẓihār, then freed the remaining half: it suffices for his expiation according to them, and according to Abu Hanifa it does not suffice because what is commanded is manumission before intercourse, so it was not found because the manumission of the half occurred after intercourse. This is based on the divisibility of manumission. According to them, it suffices because of the indivisibility of manumission according to them as before, so freeing half is freeing the whole, as if the manumission of the slave occurred before intercourse. The remaining half: i.e., the other half, also does not suffice. No: the answer for the two issues, i.e., it does not suffice for the expiation. The other half: if he was wealthy, that is not allowed. Or freed half his slave etc.: this is a second issue from.
Source pages p. 485

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq explains three scenarios for freeing slaves as expiation (kaffarah) for ẓihār, an ancient form of divorce requiring expiation. The three scenarios check if partial freeing of a slave suffices for the expiation. The first scenario: a man frees half his slave for expiation and later frees the other half. This is valid by agreement if no intercourse occurs between the two acts. If intercourse does occur, Abu Hanifa holds it invalid because manumission is divisible (tajazzu al-‘itq), so the first freeing is only a partial performance, and the second half comes after intercourse, violating the condition that freeing must precede intercourse. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold manumission indivisible, so the first half constitutes freeing the entire slave, thus the condition is met from the start. The second scenario: freeing half of a jointly owned slave while the husband is wealthy and guarantees the partner's share. Abu Hanifa deems it invalid because the defect (remaining slavery) persists in the partner's share; the Sahibayn deem it valid because the guarantee transfers ownership and the manumission is without compensation if wealthy. The third scenario: freeing half, then intercourse, then freeing the other half. Again, Abu Hanifa says invalid due to divisible manumission (the second half is after intercourse), while the Sahibayn say valid due to indivisibility. The passage thus highlights the fundamental ikhtilāf over the nature of manumission.

Key Terms
ظهار (ẓihār): A form of divorce where the husband says to his wife 'you are to me like my mother's back', making marital relations forbidden until expiation is performed.
عتق (‘itq): Manumission of a slave, a form of expiation for ẓihār.
تجزؤ العتق (tajazzu’ al-‘itq): The quality of being divisible; whether freeing part of a slave counts as freeing a portion or the whole.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn, why is freeing half a slave before intercourse and the other half after intercourse valid for ẓihār expiation?
A) Because the condition of freeing before intercourse only applies to the first half.
B) Because manumission is indivisible, so the first half frees the entire slave.
C) Because the husband can guarantee the second half later.
D) Because intercourse does not affect the expiation.

Key Takeaway
The intra-Hanafi dispute on the validity of partial slave manumission for ẓihār expiation turns on whether manumission is divisible; the relied-upon position (Sahibayn) holds it indivisible, making the first half sufficient.

Slave's Dhihar Expiation: Only Fasting Permitted
Ruling on slave's dhihar expiation limited to fasting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a slave's dhihar expiation and explain why only fasting is valid.

Core Idea
A slave who performs dhihar can only expiate by fasting, because he is not a property owner and cannot feed or free.

This lesson addresses a specific scenario in dhihar expiation: when the person who performed dhihar is a slave. The Hanafi school rules that the slave's expiation is limited to fasting, even if his master offers to feed or free on his behalf. Understanding this ruling requires grasping the legal capacity of a slave to own property (ahliyyat al-milk).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is a slave performing dhihar. The ruling is that expiation is wajib, but the slave's options are restricted.
2
Locate the specific restriction
The text states: 'ولم يجز للعبد إلا الصّوم' – it is not permissible for the slave except fasting.
3
Analyze the reason (talil)
Why only fasting? Because the slave is not ahl al-milk (owner of property), so he cannot give food or free a slave. Even if his master does it on his behalf, it is invalid.
4
Compare with general expiation options
For a free man, three options: fasting, feeding sixty poor, freeing a slave. For a slave, only fasting remains.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Maliki scholar Abu al-Qasim permits feeding with master's permission; the Hanafi school does not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولم يجز للعبد إلا الصّوم وإن أطعم أو أعتق عنه سيده، فإن لم يستطع لأنه لا مال له متصلة أي عن جهة العبد المظاهر الحر بيان كفارة الظهار الصوم ستين فقيرا كالفطرة، أو قيمته، فلو أمر غيره أن يطعم عنه من ظهاره ففعل صح = في قدر الواجب وفي المصرف أي المظاهر أي نائباً عنه أطعم عن كفارته ولهذا لو جامعها في خلال الإطعام لا يستأنف وللطرفين: أن النص يقتضي تقديم الصوم على الوطء، وأن يكون الصوم خالياً عن الوطء، فإذا فات التقديم وسقط لتعذره وجب أن يأتي بالآخر وهو الإخلاء؛ لأن العجز يوجب سقوطهما، بخلاف الإطعام؛ لأنه غير مقيد بالتقديم، وقيد بكفارة الظهار؛ لأن في كفارة عن أحدهما لا العبد عن من الوطئ فيها لمعنى يختص بالصوم. (فتح عيني) القتل لو وطئ ناسياً لا يستأنف؛ لأن المنع ولم يجز للعبد: [ولو مكاتباً في كفارة الظهار أو غيرها. (ط) أي لو ظاهر العبد من امرأته وأراد الكفارة عن الظهار لم يجز له إلا الكفارة بالصوم، ولو أطعم نائباً عنه مولاه؛ لأنه ليس من أهل الملك، فلم يكن أهلاً للتكفير بالمال، وليس للمولى منع التكفير بالصوم لتعلق حق المرأة به بخلاف سائر الكفارات، وإنما لم تتنصف؛ لما فيها من معنى العبادة (مستخلص فتح سيّده أي مولاه ولو بإذنه وهو واصل بما قبله، وعند أبي القاسم المالكي: لو أطعم بإذن المولى جاز. (ع)
And it is not permissible for the slave except fasting, even if his master feeds or frees on his behalf, for he cannot, because he has no property connected to him. Meaning from the side of the slave, the free man who performs dhihar. Explanation of the expiation of dhihar: fasting, sixty poor people like fitr, or its value. And for both sides: that the text requires precedence of fasting over intercourse, and that fasting be free from intercourse. Source pages p. 487

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on dhihar expiation for a slave. The Hanafi position is that a slave who performs dhihar may only expiate by fasting, not by feeding or freeing slaves, because he is not a property owner (ahl al-milk). Even if his master feeds or frees on his behalf, it is not valid. The text also clarifies that a mukatab (slave contracted to earn freedom) is treated the same. The master cannot prevent the slave from fasting, as the wife's right is attached. Unlike other expiations, the slave's fasting is not halved (i.e., a slave normally reduces expiation by half, but here it is not halved because of the worship aspect). The passage also discusses the ruling if the one expiating has intercourse during the period of feeding: he does not restart the feeding, because feeding is not tied to precedence, unlike fasting which must be free of intercourse. The commentary cites Fath al-‘Ayni and notes a Maliki opinion that feeding with the master's permission is valid, contrasting with the Hanafi view.

Key Terms
ظهار (dhihar): A form of divorce-like pronouncement where a man says to his wife 'you are to me like the back of my mother,' requiring expiation before resuming marital relations.
مكاتب (mukatab): A slave who has a contract with his master to earn his freedom by paying installments.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Fasting for two consecutive months
D) Any of the above with master's permission

Key Takeaway
A slave's dhihar expiation can only be fulfilled by fasting, because he cannot own property to feed or free.

Amount and Value in Dhihar Expiation
Rulings on amount, value payment, and deputizing in dhihar expiation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the amount and value payment in dhihar expiation, and explain the proof from hadith and the differences with other schools.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school requires half a sa' of wheat or one sa' of dates/barley per poor person in dhihar expiation and permits paying market value.

This passage details the specific amounts for feeding in dhihar expiation, drawing on the hadith of Salamah bin Sakhr. It also addresses the permissibility of paying monetary value instead of food, mixing different types of staple foods, and deputizing another to perform the feeding. Understanding these details is crucial for correctly fulfilling the expiation and avoiding common pitfalls.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Determine the act being ruled upon: feeding sixty poor persons as expiation for dhihar. State the ruling: it is wajib (obligatory).
The ruling level is wajib, not fard, because the proof is a hadith ahad (zanni al-thubut).
2
Locate the dalil
Find the primary evidence cited: the hadith of Salamah bin Sakhr al-Bayadhi, reported by Abu Dawud and al-Tirmidhi, where the Prophet ordered feeding a wasq of dates among sixty poor people.
A wasq equals 60 sa' in volume.
3
Derive the amount from the dalil
From the hadith, derive the amount per poor person: 60 sa' ÷ 60 = 1 sa' of dates. The Hanafis then interpret that 1 sa' of dates is equivalent in food value to half a sa' of wheat, hence the option of half a sa' of wheat or one sa' of dates/barley.
This equivalence is based on customary value in the Hanafi school.
4
Note the ikhtilaf with other schools
Compare the Hanafi ruling with the Shafi'i (1 mudd), Maliki (2 mudds), and Hanbali (1 mudd wheat/2 mudds dates) positions. Also note the disagreement on paying value (qimah) – Hanafi permits, others forbid.
The thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference) is the actual amount and the ability to substitute cash.
5
Understand rulings on mixing and deputizing
Analyze the permissibility of mixing types (e.g., wheat and barley) within the same genus, and the validity of asking another person to feed on one's behalf.
The key principle: completion by parts but not by value; deputizing is valid by analogy to explicit agency.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أطعم ستين فقيراً: أي أطعم كل مسكين نصف صاع ولا يجوز في سائر الكفارات أن يعطي الواحد أقل من نصف صاع؛ لأن العدد منصوص عليه في الكفارة فيجب عليه نصف صاع من بر أو صاع من تمر أو شعير؛ لقوله عليها السلمة بن صخر البياضي: "أطعم ستين مسكيناً وسقاً من تمر بين ستين مسكيناً"، رواه أبوداود والترمذي، وقال: حديث حسن، وعند الشافعي الله لكل مسكين مداً من غالب قوتِ بلده، براً كان أو غيره، وعند مالك: مداً بمد هشام، وهو مدان بعد النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وعند أحمد: من البر مداً، ومن تمر أو شعير مدين. [رمز الحقائق: ٢٨٥/١] ولو دفع البعض من الحنطة والبعض من الشعير جاز، وكذا يجوز نصف صاع من دقيق البر أو سويقه أو زبيب. (فتح) أو قيمته [ أي أو أعطى قيمته مقدار الفطرة من غير الأعداد المنصوصة. (ط)] أي دفع قيمة الطعام المذكور من غير ما نص عليه، وعند الثلاثة: لا يجوز دفع القيمة، وقد مر الأصل في الزكاة ويجوز تكميل أحد النوعين بالآخر لاتحاد المقصود، وهو الإطعام فصار جنساً واحداً من هذا الوجه، فجاز التكميل بالأجزاء، ولا يجوز بالقيمة، حتى لو أدى أقل من صاع من التمر يساوي نصف صاع من بر لا يجوز؛ لأن القيمة لا تعتبر في المنصوص عليه، فصار كما لو أدى نصف صاع من تمر جيد يساوي صاعاً من الوسط حيث لا يجوز. [رمز الحقائق: ٢٨٦/١] لأن العبرة في المنصوص عليه بعين النص لا لمعناه، وعليه أن يتم للذين أعطاهم ما قدر من ذلك الجنس، فإن لم يجدهم استأنف الإطعام. (فتح) صح: أي لو أمر المظاهر غيره أن يطعم نيابة عنه لأجل كفارة الظهار ففعل الغير صح عن كفارته؛ لأنه طلب من الغير التمليك معنى، والفقير قابض له أولاً ثم لنفسه، فتحقق تملكه، ثم تمليكه كما لو أمره صريحاً بالقبض فقبضه .
He fed sixty poor people: i.e. he fed each poor person half a sa', and it is not permissible in other expiations to give one less than half a sa', because the number is specified in the expiation. So it is obligatory upon him half a sa' of wheat or a sa' of dates or barley, due to his saying (peace be upon him) to Salamah bin Sakhr al-Bayadhi: 'Feed sixty poor people with a wasq of dates among sixty poor people,' reported by Abu Dawud and al-Tirmidhi, who said: a good hadith. And according to al-Shafi'i: for each poor person a mudd of the predominant staple of his country, whether wheat or otherwise. According to Malik: a mudd by the mudd of Hisham, which is two mudds after the Prophet (peace be upon him). According to Ahmad: from wheat one mudd, and from dates or barley two mudds. And according to the three (other schools): it is not permissible to pay the value, and the principle has passed in zakat. And it is permissible to complete one type with the other due to the unity of the purpose, which is feeding, so it becomes one genus from this perspective, so completion by parts is permissible, but not by value. Even if he gives less than a sa' of dates equal to half a sa' of wheat, it is not permissible, because value is not considered in what is specified, so it becomes like if he gave half a sa' of good dates equal to a sa' of medium, where it is not permissible. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 1/286] Because the consideration in what is specified is the specific item itself, not its meaning. And he must complete for those to whom he gave what was determined from that genus; if he does not find them, he restarts the feeding. (Fath) It is valid: i.e. if the one who performed dhihar ordered someone else to feed on his behalf for the expiation of dhihar, and the other did it, it is valid for his expiation, because he requested from the other the meaning of ownership transfer, and the poor person first takes for him (the deputy) then for himself, so his ownership is realized, then his transferring ownership, as if he explicitly ordered him to take possession and he took possession.
Source pages p. 487

Commentary
This passage details the method of feeding in dhihar expiation. The Hanafi ruling is that each of the sixty poor persons must receive half a sa' of wheat or one sa' of dates or barley. The proof is the hadith of Salamah bin Sakhr al-Bayadhi where the Prophet ordered feeding a wasq of dates among sixty poor people, which yields half a sa' per person. The text compares with other schools: Shafi'i requires one mudd, Maliki two mudds, Hanbali one mudd of wheat or two mudds of dates/barley. The Hanafi view is that paying the monetary value (qimah) instead of food is permissible, contrary to the three other schools. However, when mixing types, completion is allowed within the same genus (e.g., wheat and barley) but not by value; for example, giving less than a sa' of high-quality dates worth half a sa' of medium wheat is not accepted because the value is not considered. If one gives incomplete amounts, he must complete for the same recipients; if they cannot be found, he restarts. The passage also validates deputizing another to feed on one's behalf, as the deputy receives the food for the poor and then transfers ownership to them.

Key Terms
صاع (sa'): A unit of volume, approximately 2.5 kg for wheat; half sa' used for wheat, full sa' for dates/barley in expiation.
قيمة (qimah): Monetary value of the specified food items paid instead of the actual food.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school specifies half a sa' of wheat or one sa' of dates/barley per poor person in dhihar expiation, permits paying value, and allows mixing types.

Ibahah vs Tamlik in Expiations: The Hanafi-Shafi'i Dispute
Hanafi distinction between ibahah and tamlik in expiations and charities

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on ibahah in expiations and fidya, compare it with the Shafi'i position, and derive the ruling from Quranic wording.

Core Idea
The Quran uses 'it'am' in expiations, which literally means enabling to eat (ibahah), not ownership transfer.

What is the difference between making food available and transferring ownership? In Islamic law, expiations and charities sometimes require one or the other. The Hanafi school draws a sharp distinction based on Quranic wording. This lesson explores that distinction and the debate with the Shafi'i school, including practical consequences and a discussion of deputization in expiations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and its Ruling
The act is providing food in expiations (kaffarat) and fidya. According to Hanafis, ibahah (making food permissible to eat) is sufficient; tamlik (ownership transfer) is not required.
2
Locate the Dalil
The Quranic verses use the word 'it'am' in expiations (58:4) and fidya (2:184). The Hanafi argument is that 'it'am' literally means enabling to eat, i.e., ibahah. For zakat and 'ushr, the words 'ita' and 'ada' are used, which imply tamlik.
Compare Quran 2:43 'Wa atu al-zakata' with 58:4.
3
Analyze the Dalil's Wajh al-Dalalah
'It'am' is a transitive verb meaning 'to make someone taste' or 'to feed'. The literal sense is simply to make food available. Tamlik is only understood by implication (dalalat al-nass), not by explicit wording.
The Hanafi usul principle: al-haqiqah tu'addalu ila al-majaz bi qarina.
4
Note the Ikhtilaf
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that tamlik is required in all such obligations because it is more relieving of need, and because 'it'am' is customarily used for tamlik. He also analogizes expiations to zakat as obligatory charities.
Shafi'i dalil is based on 'urf and qiyas.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi Response
The Hanafi response: the literal meaning of 'it'am' is tamkin (enabling), which is ibahah. Tamlik is permissible by implication but not required. The Shafi'i analogy to zakat fails because the Quranic wording differs. Moreover, acting on the implication does not negate the literal meaning, just as the prohibition of 'uff' implies prohibition of hitting but does not remove the literal prohibition of 'uff'.
The response uses the example of Quran 17:23 to illustrate that implication does not override literal meaning.

وتصح الإباحة في الكفارات والفدية دون الصدقات والعشر، والشرط غداءان فلا ثم أمر بأن يصرفه إلى نفسه كفارة، وليس للمأمور أن يرجع على الآمر في ظاهر الرواية؛ لأنه يحتمل الهبة والقرض، بالشك، وعن أبي يوسف عليه أنه يرجع؛ لأنه وإن احتمل الهبة إلا أن القرض أدناهما ضرراً فتحمل يرجع الأمر عليه، وإنما قيد بقوله: "أن يطعم عنه"؛ لأنه لو قال لغيره: "أعتق عبدك عن ظهاري" ففعل، لا يسقط عن عند الطرفين خلافاً لأبي يوسف، وإن أعتق عنه بغير أمره لم يجز اتفاقاً لوقوع العتق عن المعتق، وإن كان الإعتاق يجعل سماه جاز اتفاقاً، ووجه عدم السقوط إذا كان العتق بأمره أن التمليك بغير بدل هبة، ولا جواز لها بدون القبض، ولم يوجد القبض في الإعتاق ووجد في الإطعام (مستخلص، فتح، عيني) وتصح الإباحة :إلخ والضابط أن ما شرع بلفظ الإطعام والطعام تجوز فيه الإباحة، وما شرع بلفظ الإيتاء والأداء يشترط فيه التمليك، فالمنصوص في الكفارات الإطعام، كقوله تعالى في كفارة الظهار: ﴿فَمَنْ لَمْ يَسْتَطِعْ فَإِطْعَامُ سِتّينَ مِسْكِينا (المجادلة:٤)، وفي الفدية قوله تعالى: ﴿وَعَلَى الَّذِينَ يُطِيقُونَهُ فِدْيَةٌ طَعَامُ مِسْكِينٍ ﴾ (البقرة: ١٨٤)، وقوله: "دون الصدقات والعشر" فإنه يشترط فيه التمليك؛ لأن المنصوص فيه الإيتاء كما في قوله تعالى: ﴿وَآتُوا الزَّكَاةَ﴾ (البقرة : ٤٣)، وقوله عليها: "أدوا العشر" بلفظ الأداء، وهو يقتضي التمليك، وقال الشافعي: يشترط التمليك في الكفارات أيضاً، ولا يعتبر الإباحة في الكل؛ لأن التمليك أدفع للحاجة، والإطعام يذكر للتمليك عرفاً، يقال: "أطعمتك هذا الطعام أي مكنتك، فيحمل عليه، أو هو مراد بالإجماع فانتفى الآخر أن يكون مراداً؛ لأن فيه الجمع بين الحقيقة والمجاز أو العموم في المشترك، وكل ذلك لا يجوز؛ ولأنها صدقة واجبة، فيكون من شرطها التمليك كالزكاة وصدقة الفطر والكسوة في كفارة اليمين. ولنا: أن المنصوص عليه في الكفارة والفدية الإطعام، وهو حقيقة في التمكين؛ لأنه عبارة عن جعل الغير طاعماً، وذلك بالإباحة، وإنما جاز التمليك بدلالة النص، والعمل بها لا يمنع ،بالحقيقة ألا ترى أن ضرب الوالدين وشتمهما يحرم بدلالة النص في قوله تعالى: ﴿فَلا تَقُلْ لَهُمَا أُفٍّ ﴾ (الإسراء:۲۳) مع بقاء الأصل مراداً، وهو بخلاف المستشهد؛ لأن المنصوص عليه فيه الإيتاء والأداء والكسوة وهي تقتضي التمليك. (عيني، فتح) أقول: الفرق بين الإباحة والتمليك أن الإباحة هو التمكين من الشيء للاستعمال فقط مثلاً: إذا أباح الطعام للفقير فله أن يأكله وليس له أن يهب الطعام المباح أو يبيعه أو يتصرف فيه بتصرف آخر، والتمليك جعل الغير مالكاً لشيء، فله أن يتصرف فيه بما شاء من الاستعمال بنفسه أو الهبة وغيرها. (محشي) التأفيف، الكفارات كفارة الظهار وكفارة الصوم وكفارة اليمين وكفارة قتل الصيد. (ع) والفدية: أي وتصح الإباحة في الفدية أيضاً مثل أجزية الجنايات في الحج وفدية الصوم للشيخ الفاني. (ط،ع) الصدقات: [فإنه يشترط فيها التمليك. (ط)] كالزكاة وصدقة الفطر والحلق عن الأذى. (مسكين) غداءان: بفتح الغين المعجمة تثنية غداء وهو طعام الضحى. (ع)
And ibahah (making permissible) is valid in expiations and fidya, but not in sadaqat and 'ushr. The condition is two lunches... then he ordered that he should spend it on himself as expiation. And the deputy is not entitled to return (to take back) from the one who ordered in the apparent narration, because it is subject to probability of gift or loan, due to uncertainty. And from Abu Yusuf that he does return, because although it may be a gift, the loan is less harmful, so the command is interpreted as return. And he restricted it to his saying "that he feed on his behalf" because if he said to another: "Free your slave on my behalf from my dhihar" and he did, it does not exempt him according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), contrary to Abu Yusuf. And if he freed on his behalf without his order, it is not permissible by agreement, because the freeing occurs from the one who frees. And if the freeing made him name him, it is permissible by agreement. The reason for non-exemption if the freeing is by his order is that ownership transfer without consideration is a gift, and it is not valid without taking possession, and possession does not occur in freeing, while it does occur in feeding. (From Mukhtasar, Fath, ‘Ayni) And ibahah is valid: etc. The rule is that what is legislated with the word of it'am (feeding) and ta'am (food), ibahah is permissible in it; and what is legislated with the word of ita' (giving) and ada' (payment), tamlik (ownership transfer) is required. So the specified wording in expiations is it'am, as in His statement in dhihar expiation: "And those who do not have the ability, then feeding of sixty poor people" (Quran 58:4), and in fidya His statement: "And upon those who are able to fast but do so with difficulty, a fidya of feeding a poor person" (Quran 2:184). And his saying: "except sadaqat and 'ushr" for in them tamlik is required because the specified wording is ita' as in His statement: "And give the zakat" (Quran 2:43), and his saying (peace be upon him): "Pay the 'ushr" with the wording of ada', which necessitates tamlik. And al-Shafi'i said: tamlik is required in expiations as well, and ibahah is not considered in any, because tamlik is more relieving of need, and it'am is customarily mentioned for tamlik; it is said 'I fed you this food' meaning I made you own it, so it is interpreted accordingly, or it is intended by consensus so the other meaning is excluded because it would be combining literal and metaphorical or common usage, which is not allowed; and because it is an obligatory charity, so its condition is tamlik like zakat and fitr and clothing in expiation of an oath. And for us: the specified wording in expiation and fidya is it'am, which is literally tamkin (enabling), because it means making the other taste, and that is through ibahah. Tamlik is only permissible due to textual indication, and acting on it does not preclude the literal meaning. Do you not see that hitting parents and insulting them is prohibited by textual indication in His statement: "Do not say uff to them" (Quran 17:23) while the original meaning remains intended. And this is different from the cited evidence because the specified wording there is ita', ada', and kiswa, which necessitate tamlik. (From ‘Ayni, Fath) I say: the difference between ibahah and tamlik is that ibahah is enabling the thing for use only: for example, if he makes food permissible to the poor person, he may eat it but he may not gift the permissible food or sell it or otherwise dispose of it. Tamlik is making the other own a thing, so he can dispose of it as he wishes, including use by himself, gift, etc. (From the glossator) al-Ta'fif, the expiations: expiation of dhihar, expiation of oath, expiation of killing game. (A) And fidya: i.e. ibahah is valid in fidya as well, such as compensation for offenses in Hajj and fidya for fasting for the elderly. (T, A) Sadaqat: [For them tamlik is required. (T)] like zakat, fitr, and shaving for harm. (Miskin) Two lunches: with fatha on the letter ghayn, dual of ghadha' which is the meal of forenoon. (A)
Source pages p. 488

Commentary
This passage establishes a key Hanafi legal principle: the distinction between ibahah (making permissible, i.e., allowing the poor to use the food without transferring ownership) and tamlik (transfer of ownership). In expiations (kaffarat) and fidya (compensations for missed fasts or Hajj), ibahah is sufficient; the giver need only make the food available for the poor to eat. However, in sadaqat (like zakat, fitr) and 'ushr (tithe on land), tamlik is required—the poor must become owners of the item. The proof is derived from Quranic wording: expiation verses use 'it'am' (feeding), which literally means making food available (ibahah), while zakat uses 'ita' (giving) and 'ushr uses 'ada' (paying), which imply ownership transfer. The text also discusses a dispute with al-Shafi'i, who requires tamlik in all. The Hanafi rebuttal uses the example of 'do not say uff to parents'—the prohibition of hitting and insulting is derived by implication from the text, not from the literal meaning, similar to how tamlik is derived by implication from 'it'am' while the literal meaning remains ibahah. The passage also covers a deputizing case: if one orders another to free a slave on his behalf for dhihar expiation, it is not valid according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, the Sahibayn) because freeing does not involve taking possession (qabd), unlike feeding where possession occurs. Abu Yusuf differs on some details. Finally, a gloss explains the practical difference: ibahah allows the poor to eat but not to dispose of the food further; tamlik allows full ownership rights.

Key Terms
إباحة (ibahah): Making something permissible for the other to use without transferring ownership; e.g., allowing a poor person to eat food at a meal.
تمليك (tamlik): Transferring ownership of a thing to another, so that the receiver can dispose of it as he wishes (e.g., sell, gift).
إطعام (it'am): Feeding; literally making someone taste food, i.e., enabling them to eat.
فدية (fidya): Compensation for missed religious obligations, such as fasting or Hajj offenses.
كفارة (kaffarat): Expiation for certain sins or broken oaths, including dhihar, broken oath, etc.
غداءان (ghada'an): Two meals; specifically two lunches (ghada').

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following requires tamlik (ownership transfer) rather than ibahah?
A) Kaffarat al-dhihar
B) Fidya for missed fasts
C) Zakat
D) Kaffarat al-yamin

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between ibahah (making food available) and tamlik (ownership transfer) based on Quranic wording: expiations use 'it'am' (ibahah), while zakat uses 'ita' (tamlik).

Ibahah vs Tamlik in Kaffarat: The Hanafi View
Ruling on permissibility of ibahah in expiations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school permits ibahah (permission to use) in feeding expiations and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument requiring tamlik.

Core Idea
The Quran's word 'it'am' means enabling to eat (ibahah), not ownership transfer (tamlik).

Feeding the poor is a common expiation in Islamic law, but does it require giving them ownership of the food or simply allowing them to eat? The Hanafi school, based on the literal meaning of 'it'am' in the Quran, holds that ibahah (permission to use) is sufficient. This lesson examines the textual evidence and the dispute with the Shafi'i school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
The passage begins: 'وتصح الإباحة في الكفارات والفدية دون الصدقات والعشر'. State the Hanafi position and the two categories of charitable obligations.
Kaffarat: expiations for zihar, oath, etc. Fidya: compensations for missed fasts, Hajj violations. Sadaqat and ushr require tamlik.
2
Locate the primary dalil
Find the Quranic verses cited: Al-Mujadilah 58:4 (kaffarat zihar) and Al-Baqarah 2:184 (fidya). Note the word 'it'am'.
The text emphasizes that the prescribed word is 'it'am', not 'ita'' (giving).
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the Hanafi school derives ibahah from 'it'am'. The Arabic root means 'to make someone taste/eat', which is achieved by enabling (tamkin) through ibahah.
Tamlik is only indicated secondarily; the primary meaning remains operative.
4
Examine the Shafi'i objection
The Shafi'i school argues that tamlik is required because 'it'am' is used customarily for tamlik, and expiation is an obligatory sadaqah similar to zakat.
They cite the need for more effective fulfillment and textual analogy with zakat.
5
Assess the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response rejects the customary override, citing that the literal meaning is preserved (like the prohibition of saying 'uff' indicates a broader prohibition). The analogy with zakat fails because zakat texts use 'ita''.
Thamarah al-khilaf: practical difference in how expiation is performed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتصح الإباحة في الكفارات والفدية دون الصدقات والعشر، والشرط غداءان فلا ثم أمر بأن يصرفه إلى نفسه كفارة، وليس للمأمور أن يرجع على الآمر في ظاهر الرواية؛ لأنه يحتمل الهبة والقرض، بالشك، وعن أبي يوسف عليه أنه يرجع؛ لأنه وإن احتمل الهبة إلا أن القرض أدناهما ضرراً فتحمل الأمر عليه، وإنما قيد بقوله: "أن يطعم عنه"؛ لأنه لو قال لغيره: "أعتق عبدك عن ظهاري" ففعل، لا يسقط عن عند الطرفين خلافاً لأبي يوسف، وإن أعتق عنه بغير أمره لم يجز اتفاقاً لوقوع العتق عن المعتق، وإن كان الإعتاق يجعل سماه جاز اتفاقاً، ووجه عدم السقوط إذا كان العتق بأمره أن التمليك بغير بدل هبة، ولا جواز لها بدون القبض، ولم يوجد القبض في الإعتاق ووجد في الإطعام (مستخلص، فتح، عيني) وتصح الإباحة :إلخ والضابط أن ما شرع بلفظ الإطعام والطعام تجوز فيه الإباحة، وما شرع بلفظ الإيتاء والأداء يشترط فيه التمليك، فالمنصوص في الكفارات الإطعام، كقوله تعالى في كفارة الظهار: ﴿فَمَنْ لَمْ يَسْتَطِعْ فَإِطْعَامُ سِتّينَ مِسْكِينا (المجادلة:٤)، وفي الفدية قوله تعالى: ﴿وَعَلَى الَّذِينَ يُطِيقُونَهُ فِدْيَةٌ طَعَامُ مِسْكِينٍ ﴾ (البقرة: ١٨٤)، وقوله: "دون الصدقات والعشر" فإنه يشترط فيه التمليك؛ لأن المنصوص فيه الإيتاء كما في قوله تعالى: ﴿وَآتُوا الزَّكَاةَ﴾ (البقرة : ٤٣)، وقوله عليها: "أدوا العشر" بلفظ الأداء، وهو يقتضي التمليك، وقال الشافعي: يشترط التمليك في الكفارات أيضاً، ولا يعتبر الإباحة في الكل؛ لأن التمليك أدفع للحاجة، والإطعام يذكر للتمليك عرفاً، يقال: "أطعمتك هذا الطعام أي مكنتك، فيحمل عليه، أو هو مراد بالإجماع فانتفى الآخر أن يكون مراداً؛ لأن فيه الجمع بين الحقيقة والمجاز أو العموم في المشترك، وكل ذلك لا يجوز؛ ولأنها صدقة واجبة، فيكون من شرطها التمليك كالزكاة وصدقة الفطر والكسوة في كفارة اليمين. ولنا: أن المنصوص عليه في الكفارة والفدية الإطعام، وهو حقيقة في التمكين؛ لأنه عبارة عن جعل الغير طاعماً، وذلك بالإباحة، وإنما جاز التمليك بدلالة النص، والعمل بها لا يمنع ،بالحقيقة ألا ترى أن ضرب الوالدين وشتمهما يحرم بدلالة النص في قوله تعالى: ﴿فَلا تَقُلْ لَهُمَا أُفٍّ ﴾ (الإسراء:۲۳) مع بقاء الأصل مراداً، وهو بخلاف المستشهد؛ لأن المنصوص عليه فيه الإيتاء والأداء والكسوة وهي تقتضي التمليك. (عيني، فتح) أقول: الفرق بين الإباحة والتمليك أن الإباحة هو التمكين من الشيء للاستعمال فقط مثلاً: إذا أباح الطعام للفقير فله أن يأكله وليس له أن يهب الطعام المباح أو يبيعه أو يتصرف فيه بتصرف آخر، والتمليك جعل الغير مالكاً لشيء، فله أن يتصرف فيه بما شاء من الاستعمال بنفسه أو الهبة وغيرها. (محشي) التأفيف، الكفارات كفارة الظهار وكفارة الصوم وكفارة اليمين وكفارة قتل الصيد. (ع) والفدية: أي وتصح الإباحة في الفدية أيضاً مثل أجزية الجنايات في الحج وفدية الصوم للشيخ الفاني. (ط،ع) الصدقات: [فإنه يشترط فيها التمليك. (ط)] كالزكاة وصدقة الفطر والحلق عن الأذى. (مسكين) غداءان: بفتح الغين المعجمة تثنية غداء وهو طعام الضحى. (ع) عشاءان: بفتح العين تثنية عشاء، طعام المساء. (ع) أو غداء وعشاء: الغداء بالفتح والمد طعام للغداة والعشاء كذلك طعام العشية، أي الشرط في طعام الإباحة إما غداءان أو عشاءان أو غداء وعشاء في يوم واحد؛ لأن المعتبر دفع حاجة اليوم، وذلك بالغداء والعشاء عادةً، ويقوم قدرهما مقامهما، فكان المعتبر أكلتين، والسحور كالغداء، ولو غدى ستين وعشى ستين غيرهم لم يجز إلا أن يعيد على أحد الستينين غداء أو عشاء، ولابد من الإدام في خبز الشعير والذرة، بخلاف خبز البر، فإذا شبعوا أجزأه قليلاً أكلوا أو كثيراً؛ لحصول المقصود، ولو كان فيهم صبي فطيم لم يجز؛ لأنه لا يستوفي كاملاً، وكذا لو كان بعضهم شبعان قبل الأكل رمز الحقائق: ٢٨٦/١] (فتح) صح: أي لو أطعم واحداً ستين يوماً أجزأه؛ لأن المقصود سد حاجة المحتاج، وقال الشافعي: لا يصح؛ لأن التفريق على الستين واجب بالنص، ولنا أن المقصود سد الحاجة والحاجة تتجدد في كل يوم، فالدفع إلى واحد في اليوم الثاني كالدفع إلى غيره من الفقراء. رمز الحقائق: ۲۸۷/۱] (مستخلص) ولو في يوم لا إلخ [ أي لو أعطى مسكيناً واحداً كل الطعام. (ع)) أي لو أعطى فقيراً واحداً ستين صاعاً في يوم واحد لم يجز إلا عن يومه ذلك؛ لأن الواجب عليه التفريق، و لم يوجد كالحاج إذا رمى الجمرة بسبع حصيات بدفعة واحدة لا يجزئه إلا عن واحدة، وهذا الحكم في الإباحة من غير خلاف، أما إذا ملك المسكين الواحد بدفعات في يوم واحد فقيل: يجوز، وقيل: لا يجوز إلا عن يومه ذلك، وهو الصحيح رمز الحقائق: ۲۸۷/۱] (مستخلص) ولا يستأنف إلخ لأن النص في الإطعام مطلق غير مقيد بما قبل المسيس، فيجري على إطلاقه، ولا يجوز حمله على النص المقيد في الإعتاق والصوم بالقياس ولا بخبر الواحد، وهو قوله علي للذي واقع امرأته قبل التكفير "استغفر الله ولا تعد حتى تكفر"؛ لأن التقييد نسخ، فلا يجوز بمثله، وإنما منع المظاهر من الوطء قبل الإطعام لجواز أن يقدر على التحرير أو الصيام فيقعان بعد الوطء، والنهي لغيره لا يعدم المشروعية، فالحاصل أن الوطء قبل الإطعام أو في خلاله وإن كان حراماً لكن لا ينافي عدم لزوم استيناف الإطعام.
