Conditions and Procedure of Li'an in Hanafi Fiqh
Describes conditions for li'an and procedure when parties refuse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for li'an and explain the Hanafi procedure when the husband refuses, including the imprisonment versus flogging dispute with the Shafi'i school.

Core Idea
Li'an replaces hadd punishments; refusal leads to imprisonment, not immediate flogging.

Li'an (mutual cursing) is a unique legal mechanism that substitutes for the hadd punishments of slander and adultery between spouses. This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq lays out the essential conditions that trigger li'an and the procedural steps when either party refuses. Understanding these rules is critical for applying family law in a Hanafi context, as the procedure differs significantly from the general law of slander.

Guided Path
1
Identify the occasion for li'an
Li'an is triggered when a husband accuses his wife of adultery or denies paternity of her child, and the wife demands its due. The passage specifies that the wife must be 'mimman yuhaddu qādhiṟuhā' – a woman whose slanderer would receive the hadd, i.e. she is chaste (muhsana). Additionally, two qualified male witnesses must be present (or the husband lacks witness qualification).
The condition of two witnesses is a qualification for the husband to initiate li'an; if he cannot produce them, he fails the condition and is punished for slander.
2
List the prerequisites for li'an
From the text, extract the conditions: (1) husband's direct accusation of adultery or denial of paternity, (2) two qualified male witnesses, (3) wife is chaste (muhsana: free, adult, Muslim, never convicted of adultery), (4) wife demands li'an. If any condition is missing, li'an is not obligatory.
The Hanafi school considers li'an a right of the wife; she may choose not to demand it, in which case the husband is not compelled to swear.
3
Trace the procedural sequence for refusal
If the husband refuses to perform li'an, the judge imprisons him until he either performs li'an or admits lying, after which he receives the hadd for slander (eighty lashes). If he performs li'an, the wife is then required to perform li'an; if she refuses, she is imprisoned until she either performs li'an or confirms the husband's accusation.
Imprisonment is a coercive measure to enforce the wife's right, not a punishment itself.
4
Analyze the Hanafi proof for imprisonment over flogging
The Hanafi position is that the general verse on slander (Qur'an 24:4) is abrogated by the li'an verses (Qur'an 24:6-9) in the spouse context. The husband's oath prevents the hadd; he is not punished until he clearly refuses or admits perjury. The opposing Shafi'i view holds the general verse applies, so refusal leads to immediate flogging.
This step requires understanding the Hanafi principle of abrogation (naskh) and the specific ruling that oaths do not establish penalties but prevent them.
5
Determine the practical effect (thamarah al-khilaf)
The practical consequence is whether the husband is flogged immediately (Shafi'i) or imprisoned first (Hanafi). The Hanafi ruling gives the husband a chance to retract and perform li'an, while the Shafi'i ruling treats refusal as a confession of slander.
This difference affects judges' practice in Hanafi jurisdictions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطلاق - باب اللعان. حد القذف في حقه، ومقام حد الزنا في حقها، فلو قذف زوجته بالزنا، وصلحا شاهدين، وهي ممن يحد قاذفها، أو نفى نسب الولد وطالبته بموجب وجب اللعان، فإن أبى حبس حتى يلاعن، أو يكذب نفسه فيحد، فإن لاعن وجب عليها اللعان، فإن أبت حُبست حتى تلاعن أو تصدقه، فإن لم يصلح الزوج شاهدا وجب الحد به عن القذف.
Book of Divorce - Chapter of Li'an. [Li'an takes] the place of the hadd of slander in his right, and the place of the hadd of adultery in her right. So if a man slanders his wife by accusing her of adultery, and there are two qualified witnesses, and she is one whose slanderer would be punished with the hadd, or he denies the lineage of the child and she demands its due, then li'an becomes obligatory. If he refuses, he is imprisoned until he performs li'an, or he admits his lie and is flogged. If he performs li'an, then li'an becomes obligatory upon her. If she refuses, she is imprisoned until she performs li'an or confirms his accusation. If the husband is not qualified as a witness, then the hadd for slander is imposed upon him.
Source pages p. 492

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq explains the essential conditions and procedural sequence of li'an (mutual cursing between spouses) in the Hanafi school. The opening states that li'an serves a dual purpose: it substitutes for the slander punishment (twenty lashes) if the husband is lying, and it substitutes for the adultery punishment (stoning or whipping) if the wife is lying. Li'an is only initiated when a husband accuses his wife of adultery in clear terms (e.g., 'You are an adulteress') or denies paternity of her child, and the wife demands that he either prove his claim or undergo li'an. Essential conditions include: the presence of two male witnesses who are legally competent to testify (i.e., free, adult, Muslim, sane, and not previously punished for slander); the wife must be 'chaste' (muhsana) – free from any valid accusation of adultery – because li'an replaces the slander punishment which only applies when the victim is chaste; and the wife must demand li'an as it is her right. If these conditions are met, the husband must perform li'an. If he refuses, the judge imprisons him until he either performs li'an or admits lying, in which case he receives the hadd for slander (eighty lashes). If the husband performs li'an, the wife is then obliged to perform li'an; if she refuses, she is imprisoned until she either performs li'an or confirms the husband's accusation. However, if the husband himself is not qualified to be a witness (e.g., he is a slave, non-Muslim, or previously punished for slander), then li'an cannot take place because he lacks the legal capacity for the oath-witnessing procedure. In that case, the hadd for slander is imposed on him directly, as the original punishment for slander applies when li'an is unavailable due to a deficiency in the husband's qualifications. The text also notes that if the wife confirms the accusation (tasdiq), she does not receive the hadd for adultery; confirmation does not amount to a confession that would obligate punishment.

Key Terms
لعان (liʿān): A procedure of mutual cursing between spouses when the husband accuses his wife of adultery or denies paternity and the wife demands proof; it substitutes for the hadd punishments.
قذف (qadhf): Accusing a chaste person of adultery; it is a crime punishable by eighty lashes (hadd al-qadhf).
ممن يحد قاذفها (mimman yuhaddu qādhiṟuhā): A woman whose slanderer would be punished with the hadd, i.e., she is chaste (muhsana), free, adult, Muslim, and never convicted of adultery.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school in this passage, what happens if the husband refuses to perform li'an after being ordered by the judge?
A) He is immediately flogged eighty lashes.
B) He is imprisoned until he performs li'an or admits lying, then flogged.
C) The marriage is automatically dissolved.
D) He is fined and released.

Key Takeaway
Li'an is a conditional substitute for hadd punishments; its procedure includes imprisonment for refusal in the Hanafi school, due to abrogation of the general slander verse by the li'an verses.

Li'an: Obligation and Consequences of Refusal (Hanafi Position)
States obligation of li'an and consequences of refusal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on what happens when a husband refuses li'an, identify the Quranic proof, and distinguish the Hanafi position from the Shafi'i position on the consequences of refusal.

Core Idea
Li'an is a substitute for hadd for spouses; refusal leads to imprisonment, not immediate flogging — the Hanafi school compels the right before punishment.

When a husband accuses his wife of zina without four witnesses, Islamic law requires li'an. But what if the husband refuses? The Hanafi school holds that he is imprisoned until he performs li'an or admits to lying, which then triggers the hadd of qadhf. This lesson unpacks this ruling, its Quranic basis, and the key dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i, who argues for immediate flogging. You will learn the legal reasoning behind the Hanafi view and its practical application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its obligation
Li'an becomes wajib upon a husband when he accuses his wife of zina without four witnesses. It is a substitute for the hadd of qadhf.
2
Locate the proof (dalil)
The Quranic verses of li'an (24:6-9) specifically address this situation and provide the procedure. The Hanafi school holds that these verses abrogate the general qadhf verse (24:4) for spouses.
3
Trace the Hanafi ruling on refusal
If the husband refuses li'an, the judge imprisons him until he either performs li'an or admits to lying, in which case he is flogged for qadhf. This coercion ensures the right is fulfilled.
4
Compare with the Shafi'i view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the husband should be flogged immediately upon refusal because li'an is a concession; refusal forfeits the concession. The Hanafi response is that the li'an verses are abrogating, not merely concessive.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The Hanafi position (imprisonment until li'an or confession) is the relied-upon view within the school, as supported by the majority of Hanafi scholars.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب اللعان وجب اللعان، فإن أبى حبس حتى يلاعن، أو يكذب نفسه فيحد، فإن لاعن وجب عليها اللعان، فإن أبت حُبست حتى تلاعن أو تصدقه، فإن لم يصلح الزوج شاهداً أي الزوج أي المرأة أي على الزوجة وهو الحد ولم يبرهن على مدعاه. (ع) اللعان عليهما؛ لأنه حق ثبت لها فيجب إقامته. (ط) أبي: أي امتنع الزوج عن اللعان. (ع) حبس حتى يلا عن [ أو تبين منه بطلاق أو غيره. (ط)] أي إن امتنع الزوج اللعان حبسه الحاكم حتى يلاعن، أو يكذب نفسه فيحد؛ لأنه حق مستحق عليه، وهو قادر على استيفائه فيحبس حتى يأتي بما عليه، أو يكذب نفسه فيرتفع السبب، وقال الشافعي له : إذا امتنع يحد حد القذف؛ لأنه وجب عليه الحد بالقذف؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿فَاجْلِدُوهُمْ (النور: ٤)، إلا أنه يتمكن من دفعه باللعان تخفيفاً عليه، فإذا لم يدفع يحد، قلنا: قذف الرجل امرأته لا يوجب الحد عند اجتماع شرائط اللعان وما تلا منسوخ في حق الزوجين بآية اللعان، ولو كان موجباً لما سقط بشهادته أو يمينه؛ لأن الحقوق لا تسقط به. (مستخلص، فتح) فيحد حد القذف لأنه امتنع عن إيفاء حق مستحق عليه. (ط،ع) أبت أي امتنعت المرأة عن اللعان. (ط) أو تصدقه فإن صدقته لا تحد حد الزنا وفي بعض نسخ "مختصر القدوري": "أو تصدقه فتحد" وهو غلط ؛ لأن الحد لا يجب بالإقرار مرة فكيف يجب بالتصديق مرة، وهو يجب بالتصديق أربع مرات؛ لأن التصديق ليس بإقرار قصداً، فلا يعتبر في حق وجوب الحد ويعتبر في درئه فيندفع به اللعان ولا يجب به الحد وعند الشافعي: إذا امتنع الزوج عن اللعان يحد وكذا المرأة إذا أبت تحد حد الزنا، وهذا عجيب منه؛ لأنه لا يقبل شهادة الزوج عليها بالزنا مع ثلاثة عدول. : ثم يوجب الحد عليها بقوله وحده، وإن كان عبداً أو فاسقاً أو كافراً، وأعجب منه أنه يمين عنده، واليمين لا يصلح لإيجاب المال ولا لإسقاطه بعد الوجوب فأسقطت المرأة به الحد ههنا عن نفسها، وكذا الزوج أسقط نفسه، وأوجب الرجم الذي هو أغلظ الحدود به على المرأة، وجعله شهادة في حقه، وهذا تناقض ظاهر، ولو صدقته في نفي الولد فلا حد ولا لعان، وهو ولدهما؛ لأن النسب إنما ينقطع حكماً باللعان، فلم يوجد، وهو حق الولد، فلا يصدقان في إبطاله رمز الحقائق: ٢٩٠/١] (فتح) الحد به عن فإن لم يصلح إلخ : يعني إذا كانت هي من أهل اللعان بأن كانت صالحة للشهادة عليه وهو لا يصلح للشهادة بأن كان كافراً ونحوه يجب عليه الحد؛ لأن اللعان تعذر لمعنى من جهته، فيصار إلى الأصل، وهو الحد الثابت بقوله تعالى: ﴿وَالَّذِينَ يَرْمُونَ الْمُحْصَنَاتِ﴾ (النور:٤)، ولا يتصور أن يكون الزوج كافراً وهي مسلمة إلا إذا كانا كافرين فأسلمت ثم قذفها قبل عرض الإسلام عليه، والأصل أن اللعان إذا سقط لمعنى من جهته فلو كان القذف صحيحاً حد وإلا فلا حد ولا لعان تبيين الحقائق: ۲۲۸/۳] (فتح) شاهداً: بأن كان كافراً أو عبداً أو محدوداً في قذف وكانت هي صالحة للشهادة. (ط،ع) حد، وإن صلح وهي ممن لا يحدّ قاذفها فلا حدّ عليه ولا لعان.
Chapter of Li'an. Li'an is obligatory. If the husband refuses, he is imprisoned until he performs li'an, or he accuses himself (confesses to lying) and is flogged with the hadd of qadhf. If he performs li'an, then li'an becomes obligatory upon the wife. If she refuses, she is imprisoned until she performs li'an or confirms his accusation. If the husband is not qualified as a witness (e.g., a slave, disbeliever, or previously flogged for qadhf), and the wife is qualified, then the husband is flogged with the hadd of qadhf. If the husband is qualified but the wife is not (e.g., she is a fornicator, minor, etc.), then there is no hadd nor li'an upon the husband. ...
Source pages p. 493

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq, with the commentary of Fath al-Qadir, establishes the rulings on li'an. It begins by stating that li'an is obligatory when a husband accuses his wife of zina without witnesses. If the husband refuses to perform li'an, the judge imprisons him until he either performs li'an or admits to lying, in which case he is flogged for qadhf. Similarly, if the wife refuses li'an after the husband has performed it, she is imprisoned until she performs li'an or confirms his accusation, which then subjects her to the hadd of zina. The Shafi'i position is presented: if the husband refuses li'an, he is flogged immediately, as the hadd of qadhf is incurred by the accusation and li'an is only a concession; refusal forfeits the concession. The Hanafi response counters that qadhf of one's wife does not mandate the hadd when the conditions of li'an are met, and the verse for qadhf is abrogated regarding spouses by the verse of li'an. Furthermore, if it were obligatory, it would not be dropped by oath or testimony, as rights cannot be waived by such means. The passage then discusses eligibility: if the husband is not qualified to testify (e.g., kafir, slave, or previously flogged for qadhf) and the wife is qualified, the husband is flogged because li'an is not possible from his side, so the default hadd applies. If the husband is qualified but the wife is not (e.g., she is a known fornicator, minor, or insane), then there is no hadd nor li'an because she is not a valid subject of testimony; the husband is punished with ta'zir. The passage ends with the principle that if either party is not eligible for testimony, the matter reverts to the original ruling: hadd for the accuser if the accusation is false, otherwise nothing.

Key Terms
اللعان (al-li'ān): Mutual imprecation between spouses when the husband accuses the wife of zina without four witnesses, consisting of four oaths each and a fifth invoking curse or wrath.
قاذف (qādhir): A person who accuses another of zina without proof (four witnesses), subject to the hadd of qadhf (80 lashes).
شاهد (shāhid): A person legally qualified to give testimony in court; for li'an, the husband must be a valid witness (free, Muslim, just, not previously flogged for qadhf).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He is immediately flogged 80 lashes for qadhf.
B) He is imprisoned until he performs li'an or confesses to lying, in which case he is flogged.
C) He is divorced from his wife automatically.
D) His accusation is accepted and the wife is stoned.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school views li'an as a substitute right for the husband; refusal results in imprisonment to coerce performance, not immediate punishment.

The Wording of Li'an Oaths
Describes the exact wording and steps of li'an

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the exact wording of the oaths in li'an as per the Hanafi school and explain why third person pointing is sufficient and preferred.

Core Idea
Li'an oaths use third person with pointing - the most definitive identification.

This lesson unpacks the specific wording of li'an oaths from Quran and Sunnah, the reasons for revelation, and a key intra-Hanafi difference that determines practice. Understanding the exact formula is crucial because deviation may invalidate the legal effect of li'an.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Quranic text
Locate the verses (An-Nur 24:6-9) that prescribe the oaths. Note the third person pronouns used for both spouses.
The Quran is the primary dalil; its wording sets the template.
2
Trace the reason for revelation
Understand the case of Hilal ibn Umayya to see why li'an was legislated as a substitute for hadd punishments.
This context clarifies the purpose: to provide an avenue for the husband when no witnesses exist.
3
Describe the husband's oaths verbatim
State the four testimonies and the fifth curse invocation exactly as given in the source, noting the pointing gesture each time.
The husband points to the wife during each oath.
4
Describe the wife's oaths verbatim
State her four testimonies and the fifth wrath invocation, again with pointing.
The wife uses 'ghadab' instead of 'la'nah'.
5
Examine the ikhtilaf on direct address
Compare the narration from Abu Hanifa (direct address, second person) with the majority view (third person with pointing). Understand the reasoning for preferring the majority view.
The majority view is mufta bibi; direct address is permissible but not required.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وصفته ما نطق به النص، أي ما ذكر الله تعالى في هذه الآيات: ﴿وَالَّذِينَ يَرْمُونَ أَزْوَاجَهُمْ (النور:1) إلى قوله تعالى: وَالْخَامِسَةَ أَنَّ غَضَبَ اللهِ عَلَيْهَا إِنْ كَانَ مِنَ الصَّادِقِينَ (النور:۹) واعلم أن سبب نزول الآية أن هلال بن أمية جاء إلى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وقال: غبت عن امرأتي سنتين فلما رجعت وجدت على بطن امرأتي شريك ابن السحماء يزني بها، فقال له علي : " انت بأربعة شهود وإلا تجلد على ظهرك " فقال هلال رأيت بعيني يا رسول الله، وأعاد هذه المقالة ثم قال: وإني لأرجو من الله أن يجعل لي مخرجاً، فأنزل الله هذه الآيات، فدل ذلك على أن اللعان قائم مقام حد القذف في حق الزوج حيث لم يجلد هلال بقذفه وقائم مقام حد الزنا في حق المرأة؛ لأنه عليها قال في آخر الحديث : لولا الأيمان سبقت لكان لي ولها شأن" فينبغي للقاضي أن يبتدئ بالزوج، فيشهد أربع شهادات، يقول في كل مرة: "أشهد بالله إني لمن الصادقين فيما رميتها به من "الزنا" يشير إليها في كل مرة، ويقول في الخامسة: "لعنة الله عليه إن كان من الكاذبين فيما رماها به من الزنا". ثم تشهد المرأة أربع شهادات تقول في كل مرة: "أشهد بالله إنه لمن الكاذبين فيما رماني به من الزنا، وتقول في الخامسة: "غضب الله عليها إن كان من الصادقين فيما رماني به من الزنا، وروى الحسن عن أبي حنيفة أنه يأتي بلفظ الخطاب، فيقول: "فيما رميتك به من الزنا ، وتقول هي: إنك" لمن الكاذبين فيما رميتني به من الزنا"، وفي ظاهر الرواية لا يعتبر الخطاب؛ لأن كلاً منهما يشير للآخر والإشارة أبلغ أسباب التعريف، والخطاب وإن كان أقطع للاحتمال لكن ضمير الغائب إذا اتصل به الإشارة ينقطع الاحتمال أيضاً، وإنما خصت هي بالغضب؛ لأن النساء يستعملن اللعن كثيراً فلا تقع المبالاة به، ويخفن من الغضب، والمراد بالنص نص الشارع يعم والسنة، أي فعل النبي عليه في عويمر العجلاني وامرأته رمز الحقائق: ٢٩٠/١]
Its description is what the text (nass) specified, meaning what Allah the Exalted mentioned in these verses: 'And those who accuse their wives [An-Nur:6]' until His saying: 'and the fifth that the wrath of Allah be upon her if he was of the truthful [An-Nur:9]'. Know that the reason for the revelation of the verse is that Hilal ibn Umayya came to the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) and said: I was away from my wife for two years, and when I returned I found on the belly of my wife Shareek ibn Salma' committing zina with her. He said: 'Bring four witnesses or else be flogged on your back.' Hilal said: I saw with my eye, O Messenger of Allah, and repeated this statement, then said: I hope that Allah will make a way out for me. So Allah revealed these verses. This indicates that li'an stands in place of the hadd of qadhf regarding the husband, as Hilal was not flogged for his accusation, and stands in place of the hadd of zina regarding the woman, because it is upon her. He said at the end of the hadith: 'Were it not for the oaths that preceded, there would have been a matter for me and her.' So it is appropriate for the judge to begin with the husband; he testifies four testimonies, saying each time: 'I testify by Allah that I am among the truthful in my accusation of her of zina,' pointing to her each time, and says the fifth: 'The curse of Allah be upon me if I am among the liars in my accusation of her of zina.' Then the woman testifies four testimonies, saying each time: 'I testify by Allah that he is among the liars in his accusation of me of zina,' and says the fifth: 'The wrath of Allah be upon me if he is among the truthful in his accusation of me of zina.' Al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa that he (the husband) comes with the wording of direct address, saying: 'in my accusation of you of zina,' and she says: 'you are among the liars in your accusation of me of zina.' In the apparent narration (zahir al-riwaya), direct address is not considered, because each of them points to the other, and pointing is the most effective means of identification, and although direct address is more decisive for possibility, the third person pronoun when accompanied by pointing also cuts off possibility. The woman is specifically mentioned with 'wrath' because women use cursing frequently so they do not take it seriously, and they fear wrath. The intended meaning of 'nass' is the text of the Lawgiver, inclusive of the Sunnah, i.e., the action of the Prophet (peace be upon him) regarding Uwaymir al-Ajlani and his wife.
Source pages p. 494

Commentary
This passage describes the procedure (sifah) of li'an as derived from the Quranic text and the practice of the Prophet. It begins by citing the relevant verses from Surah An-Nur (24:6-9), which prescribe the oaths. The reason for revelation is given: Hilal ibn Umayya accused his wife of zina with a specific man, and the Prophet initially demanded four witnesses. When Hilal could not produce them, li'an was revealed as a substitute. This establishes that li'an replaces the hadd of qadhf for the husband and the hadd of zina for the wife. The judge begins with the husband, who swears four times: 'I testify by Allah that I am among the truthful in my accusation of her of zina,' pointing to her, and a fifth time: 'The curse of Allah be upon me if I am among the liars.' The wife then swears four times: 'I testify by Allah that he is among the liars in his accusation of me of zina,' and a fifth time: 'The wrath of Allah be upon me if he is among the truthful.' The passage notes an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: according to a narration from Abu Hanifa, the oath should be in direct address (second person), but in the zahir al-riwaya (apparent transmission), the third person with pointing is sufficient and actually more definitive. The reason for the wife's fifth statement using 'ghadab' (wrath) instead of 'la'nah' (curse) is psychological: women are accustomed to cursing, so they might not fear a curse, but they fear wrath. The passage concludes that the 'nass' (text) refers to both Quran and Sunnah, citing the case of Uwaymir al-Ajlani as further proof.

Key Terms
الشهادات الأربع (al-shahādāt al-arba‘): The four testimonies (oaths) sworn by each spouse during li'an, affirming or denying the accusation of zina.
اللعنة (al-la‘nah): The fifth statement of the husband: 'The curse of Allah be upon me if I am among the liars.'
الغضب (al-ghaḍab): The fifth statement of the wife: 'The wrath of Allah be upon me if he is among the truthful.'

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the fifth statement of the husband in the li'an procedure according to the protocol described?
A) 'The wrath of Allah be upon me if I am among the liars.'
B) 'The curse of Allah be upon me if I am among the liars.'
C) 'I am truthful in my accusation.'
D) 'May Allah forgive me.'

Key Takeaway
The li'an procedure follows the Quranic wording verbatim; third person pointing is the relied-upon Hanafi practice for delivering the oaths.
